Recommended
14.6 hrs on record
Posted: 13 December, 2019
Quick Summary
Devil May Cry 5 (DMC5) is an excellent game that has a very in-depth combat and skills, along with a high skill ceiling. It also sports gorgeous visuals thanks to the RE engine, and various characters that all play differently and keep the whole thing feeling fresh. Environments are varied with hidden secrets, challenges, and alternative routes. The cutscenes are just as high quality as the gameplay itself, with a variety of interesting characters and interesting twists.

Pros
Fantastic graphics and visuals
Great optimization
An absolute banger of a soundtrack, that fits the game perfectly
Huge variety of enemies and bosses
Very in-depth combat system with tons of skills and weapons to unlock and upgrade
Interesting story with unique and memorable characters
Highly replay-able

Cons
One character is very simplistic to play
For new comers, the skills and different characters can be overwhelming
Some of the combat arenas become predictable
Any key skips a cutscene with no warning (including tab + shift for steam overlay)
Camera angle with keyboard and mouse is often janky

Story
*No Spoilers* DMC5 has a pretty interesting story that most players will appreciate after having played the previous games. However, for newcomers, it’s still fairly easy to follow as the game has a fairly lengthy introductory cutscene, along with gradual tutorials that also give you lore at the same time. All of the characters are well developed and playing as different ones at varying times in the story adds a lot to the experience as well.

Having plenty of cutscenes was a nice change of pace from all the murder and mayhem, as fun as that was. Overall, the story in DMC is very well done and ties into the old games, but is still accessible to newcomers (though players would benefit from watching a synopsis at least).

Gameplay
This is where the meat of this game is. And also, where you will take a lot of meat out of demons (because hey, they deserve it). The gameplay in DMC5 is smooth, brutal, and requires fast reflexes. It feels like riding a roller coaster that you’re not wearing a seat belt on… increasingly exciting and invigorating, but if you lose control and thus your groove, you will be punished.

One additional note is that the game seems to encourage multiple playthroughs, since you cannot unlock everything the first time through and you unlock additional modes or further upgrades upon your first campaign completion. The gameplay can roughly be divided into a few categories, though with some overlap: Combat, Skills, Items, and Exploration.

The combat
The combat in DMC5 is essentially third person hack and slash with lots of different combos or skills you can utilize. A very important fact to keep in mind is that combat varies greatly between characters as well, so you can expect a large amount of variety. The battles primarily take place inside a locked arena (similar to Doom 2016) which means there is truly no escape, and you must fight to the death. There are a few roaming enemies throughout the course of the game but most of the battles are very focused, intentional events. Correctly making combo moves and switching up attack styles quickly results in a higher score in your missions, with the highest being “SSS”.

Most combat consists of a primary attack using some sort of melee weapon (like a sword or fists), with a secondary attack that is often ranged (like a revolver or shotgun). Another important element is the “lock-on” feature that lets you concentrate on a specific enemy, and which also acts as a modifier for certain attacks. In addition, enemy attacks can often be countered or dodged with the correct time and combination of keys.

Skills
Branching out from these basic attacks, are skills and movements you can unlock that all can be affected by different keys or buttons. A single primary attack can be totally different by simply using your forward action or reverse action, or holding lock on with a movement key. The upgrade system really goes insanely in-depth here, providing the player the opportunity to really experiment and find the skills they enjoy. Skills are unlocked with red orbs which are essentially in-game currency, that is dropped from kills and can also be found scattered throughout the maps.

As the game progresses, a lot of new and different ultimate skills can be unlocked, that push the combat ability to the max. Depending on the character, some truly devastating powers can be unleashed that knock all but the most powerful demons into bits. These ultimate powers however take time to charge and can be replenished in various but limited ways.

Items
DMC5 also allows item utilization to aid players in beating it. For instance, there are certain orbs you can pick up that restore your health, or permanently upgrade it. One orb will revive you on the spot if you die in a battle. This does however reduce your score level in the mission. There are various weapons and items you can select from before you start a mission, essentially customizing your loadout.

Exploration
Finally, exploration actually plays a pretty significant part in DMC5. For all the vicious combat and lively action, there is a surprising amount of hidden secrets that reveal extra missions or items. Also, there are a few small environmental puzzles that you need to figure out to progress, but they are nothing complicated. Often times, exploration will really help with future battles since you can find important upgrades or even replenish health before a boss.

Graphics and Visuals
Graphics and optimization are where DMC5 really shines. The character faces and animations are impeccable, and the environments are detailed with fantastic atmosphere. The combat is only made better because of this, as there is nothing quite like seeing high resolution demon blood flying across the screen!

Sound
DMC5 has very well-designed audio, with lots of audio cues and combat that provides plenty of feedback. The only audio-related aspect that really stood out in a good way, was the soundtrack. DMC5 frankly has an amazing soundtrack, with really memorable tracks that fit perfectly to the high intensity combat. Another cool detail is the music intensity increases with the score the player racks up during combat. I still find myself playing the songs after completing the game and headbanging along with them.

Bugs, Glitches and Crashes
I did experience one bug with the game. After using Steam overlay, a couple times the game wouldn’t fully recognize my input and so I couldn’t move or switch weapons. I had to reload a checkpoint to get around this. Another technical complaint I have is that the cutscenes will skip with the press of any key, so keep your fingers off the keyboard if you want to watch the cutscenes. However, you CAN re-watch cutscenes from the main menu.

Price… is it worth it?
DMC5 is currently listed at $59.99, which is typical for a newer AAA game. For true fans of the DMC franchise, this price is easily worth it because of how re-playable the game is and a decently long campaign. For newcomers such as myself, I got the game on the most recent sale for $19 which was definitely a bargain for the high-quality experience.

Conclusion
In conclusion, DMC5 seems to be a nearly flawless addition to the DMC franchise with lots of fluid and technical combat, an intense story, and absolutely gorgeous visuals. For someone completely new to the franchise and even to the genre, it is worth picking up on sale and obliterating some demons.

Follow our curator page, Alexander's Club Curations if you like and want to see more reviews like this one.

Recommended
3,097.9 hrs on record
Posted: June 20
Hey! To whoever reading this, thank you so much! It's not often that I pour this many hours (2,889) into a game, so you know Devil May Cry 5 is truly special! This game, in my opinion, is not only the best Devil May Cry game, but also the greatest character action and hack n' slash game of all time! There isn't a single game that offers nearly as much combat depth as DMC5. There are many ways to extend combos, whether you're airborne, animation/jump canceling to chain different moves together in rapid succession, stance/style switching while juggling multiple weapons, etc.

You truly feel like you have all the freedom to play how you want! The player expression rocks. DMC5 feels like an amazing 3D fighting game actually. The move sets for every character are so huge and expansive, and with the inclusion of mods (I recommend downloading them from Nexus Mods), you'll never get bored and will forever be addicted, captivated, impacted and entertained! Combat for DMC has always been one of its strongest suits, and it's definitely the best it's ever been in 5. The gorgeous RE graphics engine also highlights just how extremely beautiful this game is! Whether you're engaged in the ultra buttery smooth combat or enjoying the awesome cutscenes/story, you can't help but be completely blown away at the level of detail that resides within DMC5.

Capcom truly poured their heart into this love letter of a title, and after waiting what felt like forever (11 years since DMC4!), the wait is truly worth it when you pop this bad boy in. Oh, and be prepared to discover ultimate motivation when you get your hands on Vergil! Vergil is a newly playable character with an incredibly exciting, haunting, and masterful theme to boot (Bury the Light). It's my new favorite song actually. That's another amazing part about this game; the music!

It's so good, that I doubt you'll be using custom soundtracks much. But anyway, that's my DMC5 review! I hope you enjoyed the read just as much as I enjoyed writing it! If you haven't played it yet, don't wait any longer! Bless the entire team at Capcom, along with Hideaki Itsuno-san, for this incredible masterpiece. DMC IS BACK!! We're all eagerly awaiting DMC6 now!!

Overall Score: 9.4 / 10

Quality	9.7/10	　　 　 　 High quality AAA title
Performance	10/10	Flawless; steady 60 fps @ 1080p on ultra
(cloned); ∅ 60 fps @ 4k, medium, AO off
Utility	10/10	No glitches, bugs or crashes experienced;
fair checkpoints; autosave; many options
Controls	9/10	Very good, but clearly meant to be played
with a gamepad; lots of individual combos
for each of the three available characters
Gameplay	9.3/10	　 　 　Spectacular hack-and-slash
Challenge	10/10	Six difficulty levels including instant-death
and limited continues; challenging bosses
with multiple phases and enrage; different
enemy attack patterns, spawns and even
new enemy skills on higher difficulty levels
Content	9/10	~15-20 h for a 100% run (bonus missions,
collectables and cutscenes); ~6 h rushed;
high replayability; future DLCs confirmed
Diversity	9/10	Different protagonists and locations keep
things fresh; ranged mage V's playstyle is
suprisingly innovative, but Nero & Dante
therefore both got huge weapon arsenals
Immersion	9/10	Intense action game with sick soundtrack,
that's hard put down again; in-game MTX
are barely noticable and never advertized
Design	9.2/10	　 　 　 　"Smoking sexy style!"
Visuals	10/10	Beautifully arranged visuals overall; many
HQ cutscenes; crazy moves (+ finishers);
impressively detailed, smooth animations
Sound	10/10	Badass, diverse OST featuring edgy music
genres, that suits the action just perfectly;
high quality SFX & voiceovers (ENG / ♥♥♥)
Texts	8/10	Intricate narration, well written dialogues
and well dozed funny moments; contains
a story summary of all the old DMC titles
& an all-embracing collection of lore docs
Mapping	9/10	Linear levels with little side areas in which
the collectables are hidden; the level size
never felt like a limiting factor though, be-
cause the stages serve as a sequence of
diverse, extensive combat arenas anyway
Interface	9/10	Neat UI overall; old fashioned, traditional
Capcom menu design (simple and clean);
satisfying, somewhat customizable HUD

Recommended
12.6 hrs on record
Posted: March 11, 2019
I NEED MORE POWER!

Introduction

Devil May Cry 5 is a brilliant comeback of the series after 11 years of wait. The game is short like all other entries with a run being around 9-12 hours but those hours are filled with an experience that people had been waiting for more than a decade to enjoy and it's worth it. While the game maintains its usual formula, it introduces new aspects to returning characters and unique playstyles. It makes each of the protagonists diversify their approach to enemies and keeps gameplay fresh even after beating the game. This might be the best Devil May Cry up to date.

Gameplay

Gameplay is a beast, players get to play as three characters: Nero, V and of course Dante. Each of them has their own unique powers, mechanics, and upgrades. There is something for everyone: Nero is like the standard version, he has simple combos, complicated ones and a huge arrange of devil breakers. V is more quiet, like Vergil in previous titles is about dominating the battlefield by keeping different enemies at bay at all times while moving at a slow pace, analyzing what the player faces before jumping in. Finally, Dante is a clear contrast to V, he is crazy, fast and deadly. With an insane amount of weapons and techniques, Dante can do everything which can lead to some amazing-mindblowing combos.

Some Notes

The game is fast paced, more so than previous entries. This makes combat more dynamic but can result in new players dodging more than they should. Some enemies can be very aggressive and tricky to beat but it's all a learning experience. Optimization is great, if you meet the recommended specs you will never fall below 60 FPS, it's solid. Early game can be a little dull but after a couple of hours, all aspects of the game start to shine.

What Makes It Special

The sequel that a lot of people thought would never see the light of the day is here, ready to please both old and new players with a new approach to the series. The game has three branches in the story, one for each protagonist and at times players can choose between which character they want to play as. For the first time, Devil May Cry features online play, with players running into each other and cooperating to beat sections, levels, and even bosses. Bloody Palace is coming as free DLC on April featuring more options for online play and more characters to play as and apparently it includes a fan favorite...

Sum up

+ Wraps a lot of fans speculations.
+ Players can run into each other and play together.
+ Free DLC post-launch, with the bloody palace and more characters.
+ The entry with more moves, combos, weapons, and upgrades in the series.
+ Keep Devil May Cry sense of humor, especially in V's and Dante's branches.
+ The story is dull at first, lacking in the profound element but it acquires that depth later in the story.
+ Each of the characters has their own playstyles, making it easy for players to find one that suits their style.

- Gold orbs can make bosses trivial.
- Some levels can feel like a labyrinth.
- Dante moveset is inconsistent until he gets all his weapons.
- Players who favor either V or Dante can reach a bump when playing as the other.
- At times, the game audio might stop for one second, ruining lip-sync for the rest of the cutscene.

Conclusion

Devil May Cry 5 is the game that fans had waited a good chunk of their life to play. It features smooth gameplay with intricating combos and that possibility of constant improvement, to reach that SSS rank or dominate the game for a section or two. Mastering the game it's rewarding and enhances the experience overall. The story answer long debating question that fans have formulated over the years and the soundtrack while different, suits the series. I dare say this is the best games in the series and a must have for everyone who calls themselves a gamer.

RedactedTrashman
82 products in account
0
61 people found this review helpful
2 people found this review funny 0

Recommended
13.0 hrs on record
Posted: January 17, 2020
There are a lot of ways to fight in video games, but how many games let you look like an absolute badass while doing it? We have a genre for that (though I’m not sure what exactly we call it), populated with titles like Bayonetta, REVENGEANCE, and of course, Devil May Cry. It’s been a long road for the series to get to this point, but it’s a very, very high point that it’s reached. Combining elements of almost all the previous games, cutting down the story to a central character conflict, and ramping up the action to preposterous heights, DMC 5 really is the culmination of decades of effort, and it shows in every polished, varied piece of the design.

Veteran demon hunter Dante and relative newcomer Nero have been hired by the mysterious V to take on a mission of unusual scope. A massive structure of clearly infernal origin is growing from the heart of a hapless city, and at the center of it is the demon Urizen. Joined by fellow hunters Trish and Lady, and backed up by the rambunctious inventor Nico, the three must battle their way inside the demon tower and put an end to Urizen. But this confrontation is only the beginning of the story, as Urizen’s unusual powers and familiar origin complicate matters. The paths of Nero, Dante, and V will cross, splinter, and combine to form a tale reaching far back into the history of the series, and providing new revelations for its major players.

Let it be known that I’m coming to DMC 5 after playing the original DMC, and the original DMC only. I missed 2, 3, 4, and the ill-fated reboot, and so more than a few references and revelations went straight over my un-stylish head. For folks like me, there is a handy video on the main menu that recaps the previous games (minus 2 and the reboot, which even the developers apparently pretend never existed) and at least fills you in on who the main characters are, if not the nitty-gritty of who killed whose relatives. From my perspective, the series has morphed dramatically over the years, leaving behind the sprawling castle of horrors on Mallet Island for discrete missions along linear paths.

We’ll talk more about levels, but the series has changed in other ways that are huge improvements. The heart of Devil May Cry is the action, and in 5 you are offered three wholly distinct ways to enjoy it in the characters of Nero, V, and Dante. Nero comes equipped with a wealth of tactical options, from his swift sword that can be revved for more damage and special moves, to his mechanical arm that can grapple enemies over to you and be launched for different powerful effects. His style is swift and high-flying, allowing you to continue combos on distant foes and mantle up the largest bosses. In stark contrast, V is a summoner character adjusted for a spectacle fighter. He has one teleport attack used to finish off wounded enemies, and three familiars taken from the bosses of the original game who do the fighting for him. It’s a wholly unique style for a game like this and one I absolutely love, managing an electric bird and a shape-shifting panther while I weave between foes and stab their essence out.

In a rather unexpected move, you don’t really get to play as Dante until about halfway through the game. In retrospect, though, I totally understand why that decision was made. If you thought Nero had plenty of combat options to keep track of, Dante has an incredible amalgamation of weapons, skills, and systems from all of the previous games. He can carry four melee and four ranged weapons, each with extensive skill lists, he has four combat styles that can be switched on the fly and impart new moves for each of his many weapons, he has two Devil Trigger modes that interact with each other, and he has a magic hat he can put on enemies. It can be hard to remember everything he does when you’re trying to parry blows, juggle foes, maintain your combo, and maximize your red orbs, and it seems like after every one of his levels you unlock something new for him.

More than anything though, it’s fun. All the chaos of enemies warping in, locking on and beating one to a pulp, remembering you have guns or rocket launchers, dodging through a storm of blades or countering a mighty slash with your own, every moment of it is thrilling, engaging, and gratifying. There are no real slogs in DMC 5, no fights that drag on too long or foes who take too much damage. Even the bosses lack that infuriating, murderous edge the originals did, with plenty of margin for error on normal difficulty and Gold Orbs on hand to keep you fighting if you’re not worried about your score. The combat is complex enough that you really have to devote yourself to it if you want to keep S ranks and above going, or want to survive more than thirty seconds on the higher difficulties. But for everyone else wanting a flashy, hilarious thrill ride, you won’t have to stress too much.

And what a ride it is! At this point, Dante and friends have perfected the art of unflappable badassery in the face of even the most formidable demons. Every one of them does the casual pace in front of deadly new foes, taunting them as if talking to a particularly unruly punk. The engine brings these characters to life as never before, with an incredible level of detail and realism for the entire cast. Enemy designs are gross and wild, and the environments tend to be just as fantastical with ruined city vistas and pulsating hell tunnels aplenty. The level design does suffer a bit around the halfway point, pulling back to very samey (if colorful) demon halls, but this is also where you get Dante to play with and he’s definitely a high point of the game. And I can’t overlook the music, which is an incredible mix of styles, from rock to classical, that fit the battles and cutscenes in ways you might never have imagined.

It’ll take you about 12-14 hours to crush your way through the game the first time, and after that you’ll have a wealth of difficulties and challenge modes to face if you need more. I’m pretty sure you will, too, whether it be more brutal combos with a motorcycle-sword, more dance numbers with Dante’s magic hat, or more hilariously bleak poetry from hopeless goth V. While DMC 5 approaches the kind of insanity you see in something like Bayonetta, it never quite reaches the same heights, instead choosing to focus on a wide variety of action and a few really choice moments. Even the story ends up being a pretty engaging tale of some of the game’s most memorable characters, rather than another romp to save the world. Devil May Cry 5 is the total package of style, substance, and pure fun that proves this series deserves to stand tall among action games.



Did you enjoy this review? I certainly hope so, and I certainly hope you'll check out more of them at https://goldplatedgames.com/ or on my curation page!

Product received for free

First let me be clear, I do NOT like Arena Style games, I've played a few over the years and never enjoyed them. Second I am typically a RPG FPS gamer and if you look at my catalog you'll see the majority of my games reflects an entirely different type of game than the DMC series. The only reason I have this game is I got it for free when I upgraded my graphics card.

OK with that out of the way. DMC 5 is the most incredible game I've played in a long time. I was actually sad to reach the end of the game and sat through the credits and played through them as well and was extremely happy to see the game start over with a few new additions to the menu.

The graphics are excellent,
the cut scenes are entertaining,
the story is well written,
The combat is fast, fun and very responsive,
The game might be a bit short but it just may be me not wanting it to end.
There are Easter Eggs all over the place and great surprises in the game.

Entertaining
Not Boring
Fast Pace
Visually sweet
Responsive mechanics
FUN!

If I could give this game 10 I would. Knowing what I know now I've placed DMC 4 and the other games on my wish list.

I highly recommend this game!

Recommended
18.8 hrs on record
Posted: November 7, 2019
Smokin' Sexy Recommended

I can say that this game is GOTY contender. Hack 'n' Slash gameplay is very satisfying. But there are some aspects that need tweak to be sexier.

D (Dismal)
Load and load of loading. While the shopping screen is fine. I hate it when I want to test the move it took time to load the testing area and then when I want to try other move I have to go back to shopping screen and wait for it to load again. But yeah. this is very minor annoyance but I wish I didn't have to spend that much time on character upgrade screen because of loading.

C (Crazy)
While I've seen worse camera in beat'em up game. This game still have some camera issue that come up with it's control. Make some platforming challenges somewhat harder (Thankfully they are optional). And sometime make it hard to have a decent vision on enemies during battle in packed spaces.

B (Badass)
The story is alright... It took interesting turn in the midgame. And then when things got climatic it swoop down to ending.

A (Apocalyptic)
Still I have to say that I like most of character interaction in this game they are very charming, especially Nico. V. is also kinda nice but I wish they get something more out of him.

S (Savage)
This game feature variety of move and fightning styles even for one character. Even V who has the least variety of move is still very fun to play as.

SS (Sick Skills)
Boss fight. They are balance and not overly overwhelming in normal difficulty. Boss fight in many beat'em up games often come with some obscure features that you have to no clue what, when or where to hit which could be annoying for someone who just want a quick challenge. But not in this game they are very clear of what and when you should hit them. And the rest is up to your reflex skill.

SSS (Smokin' Sexy Style)
Graphics are top notch. Animation and effect make satisfying hack 'n' slash gameplay. If it tweak some control it would be perfect.

Recommended
20.3 hrs on record
Posted: March 10, 2019
After 11 years, DMC has come to take the throne back.

My absolute favorite in the series, elevating every entry that came before it with it's emotional storytelling and unforgettable moments, with a tight, diamond cut fighting system with more depth and variety than ever before, made on Capcom's REngine which is absolutely gorgeous, the way character's facial expressions change and hair moves around mid gameplay, spectacularly intricate particle systems, an impressive roster of distortion and lighting effects perfectly mixing the over the top action with the often morphing, surreal environments and photorealistic visuals.
And it runs like a dream on PC, even on launch day.

I would have never imagined that a new DMC game would be able to out shine it's classic predecessors, but Capcom managed to do just that, solidifying the series as the king of the genre it created, directed by the man who perfected it.
They made this game for the fans, and it shows.

Recommended
1,269.4 hrs on record
Posted: March 28, 2019
Product received for free

900 hours clocked in now, game is still sick hoho merry christmas


Vergil DLC - WORTH THE DAMN 5 BUCKS. Like seriously, I thought we were going to just get a Boss Vergil with just some less awkward movement controls but nah, it's a full blown complete Vergil w/ 3 weapons, more moves & taunts compared to his old iterations. Also i'm happy for M19 - M20 and the new cutscenes are like sick af, but pre rendered hold em little bit back :sadge:


(Updated some stuff below)

Story -

Pros
- If you want the FULL story experience, read the Before the nightmare novel first. It makes the story even more fleshed out and gives so much context to the story and has little dialogues that can't be find in the game.

Visions of V is a MUST read after DMC5's story, it's pretty much how most of the cutscenes would have went if DMC5 were given more budget LuL AND we get to see an actual prequel of dante & vergil as kids, exploration of Vergil/V's psychology before & during the events of DMC5, and shows how redgrave city went down during the invasion, and also the DMC5 Artbook to get some context on some locations and etc.

- You might emotional in the ending
- It got some sick ass small subtle details on cutscenes
- A LOT of callbacks from the old games
- Cutscenes are top notch
- Music has a lot of sick tracks

Cons
- Some Qlipoth levels are bit meh, but other than that, everything looks good imo.
- I like everything about the story, my only gripes w/ it is that it lacks some cuhrazy choreographed fights on some cutscenes when compared from DMC3 - 4 (Vergil DLC sorta fixed this because good lord the action on those new cutscenes are PERFECTO), the ending was a bit rushed, and kinda got annoyed some mistranslations on some dialogues but that's just how most ♥♥♥ games getting localized roll these days.

Gameplay -

Pros
- What I like about it is that the animations are sick, the details on some weapons are really cool, taunts are SSS tier, buster animations are still satisfying af, the game's combat is still deep af, it brings new good ♥♥♥♥ in the table, it gave dante new weapons, new mechanics, and for Nero, he has 8 devil breaker arms, new moves from his existing moveset, and a new mechanic too. V is the most interesting to play as, but I wished he was more fleshed out and was given more moveset and summons.

Cons
- If you are an advance player from dmc3 and dmc4, you might find some mechanics underwhelming or dumbed down. Enemy step has an animation cooldown now and the timing is no longer strict, you can spam jump and attack and get some consistent jc attacks, no inertia, no reversals, and some moves have a lot of recovery like royal guard and etc.
- Where. Is. My. Turbo. Mode.
- I wish there was more options for the player to tinker around like removing/lessen camera shake, no slow mo's, remove hud, and etc.
- Make the final boss a lot more aggressive pls :(

(None of these combat cons are still fixed aside from Turbo after Vergil DLC or DMC5SE sad leyf)

Graphics -

Beautiful. AF.

Recommended
14.8 hrs on record
Posted: March 7
This is my first DMC, and admittedly, it shouldn't have been.

The story is simple enough, but I feel as though a better connection and understanding would more at grasped if I played the previous entries. Other than that, combat is stylish and intense. Only downfall, to me at least, is that I found myself when surrounded by enemies, targeting only one. I wish there were more moves to counter being surrounded, perhaps there is, but most of the moves I saw and unlocked only called for locking onto one specific target. Story is okay, like again, I'm sure if I played previous DMCs, it would be more satisfying to journey through. Visuals are outstanding and the optimization is fantastic. The soundtrack is epic and unforgettable, so crank it all the way up.

Overall, I only recommend this game to players who have played other DMCs in the past. I wish I did, it would make my experience much more enjoyable, but still recommending it because it's a neat and fun game.

Recommended
99.6 hrs on record
Posted: November 24, 2021
Short: I was unable to play any 3d combat game without feeling like it's somewhat bad after playing this game. It literally ruined my taste in combat by being so stylish.

I came into this series almost blind, just into this game. The story made sense in a weird way, it's made so that a new player will feel as if they just came into this world that has it's own story running (which is how Nero, the main protagonist, feels like).
It's short, but man is it worth it. Replay value is high with wanting to both improve yourself, replaying the story, replaying on a higher difficulty, playing the Bloody Palace (Fight 101 rooms of enemies to unlock a spicy taunt), playing as the DLC character which is all the previous things but again.

My problems:
-It's rather short.
-The story, despite ending nicely, makes you want more.
-The multiplayer system is interesting, but it being only a major thing in two missions and you being instantly disconnected if you open the menu kind of sucks. I wish the next game has co-op for all the missions for even more replay value.
-The cutscenes will skip if you press any button, while not being a problem for replays it can be annoying on the first.
-The DLC character, despite being great, could have been better with one move. And he only got one and a half new bosses instead of 2 unique bosses.

OST, amazing.
Graphics, amazing.
Me, motivated.

"He who reads this far into a review but buys not, breeds pestilence.", so it is written.

Mojo
370 products in account
15
31 people found this review helpful
5 people found this review funny 0

Recommended
38.8 hrs on record
Posted: November 27, 2019
This was my GOTY 2019 for a couple of reasons. Honestly, there's not much to say that hasn't been said already about it, it is definitely Devil May Cry, back at its best, I'd even go as far as to say this is THE BEST dmc game ever made (ask me that in about 10 years from now, we'll see). Got my hopes up for more like this, definitely a great purchase, and an amazing game.

Oh? reviewing, right... So, gameplay, hack'n'slash done right, Every Combo is really satisfying, although i would say you get SSS ranks really easily this time around (V is the SSS mash buttons to win character for sure)

Music is really awesome as well. At first i was kinda distracted by the main song being a bit different, but it fits so well, and it's so good, it's on my playlist for when I go out to jog!

Graphics are RE Engine, very lifelike, pretty colors but kinda dark. Sets a good tone for the story and its characters.

And characters? Well, Deadweight Nero is back, and more badass than ever! V is a solid new addition, sometimes almost comical how much goth he is, kinda reminds me of the goth kids in South Park. Don't really need to talk about Dante, right? Main man of the franchise, he's the same good OLD Dante, in every way of the word, really. he's really old now.

Not much downsides I can see here if i'm honest, you'll want a nice pc to run this game to its perfection, Combos are easier to pull off, I guess hardcore fans may not like that ? I really don't remember playing this and going:: "that really sucks" at any point in the game.

I highly recommend this game, even for newcomers of the series, cause why not! i'm just really happy for Devil May Cry to be back and better than ever.

legendofawesome
73 products in account
0
61 people found this review helpful
6 people found this review funny 0

Recommended
15.4 hrs on record
Posted: May 20, 2020
Nico spin-off please

I'm not a fan of such games, i'm too old for this ♥♥♥♥, I just can't keep up with extremely fast gameplay anymore. But I loved it and i'll try to be unbiased here.
I didn't like previous DMC title. Although it was developed by one of my favorite studios I couldn't get into it. Not because I struggled or anything, it just felt boring and besides soundtrack i couldn't see anything good in it. Now DMC 5 is whole different thing. Bought because of good graphics and i was pleasantly surprised how enjoyable this game is.

The story is simple but pretty interesting for such game. Of course there's a lot of crazy over the top moments and humor. Everything action game should have story-wise.
Character design is great, especially Nico, damn she's hot. All 3 main characters are bad-ass how they should be.
Gameplay is practically a non-stop action with crazy moves and combos with occasional high quality cut-scenes. There are 20 levels and 3 characters to play with. For most of the game you can't choose your character so you play with either Nero, Dante or V. Some levels let you choose the character. If I recall correctly one level lets you choose from 3 and two more levels lets you choose from 2 characters.
Each character is different, has different fighting techniques, skills and moves. So basically every single level feels fresh because you either unlock new fight moves/skills or play with a different character. You will never get bored playing this game.

Fighting requires quick reaction and reflexes, the game is fast. You can execute all kinds of combos and attacks to smash the enemies which requires skill. But dear casual friends don't worry, there's a noob/casual mode and difficulty levels for you so that basically anyone could play the game. Noob mode how I call it does combos and fighting for you. What you need to do is mash the buttons randomly and the game connects those into effective attacks so you don't need to worry about remembering button combinations and such. As I said great fro slower people like me or ones who want to get used to the game first.
Speaking of enemies. The enemy design is amazing. Great selection of all kind of enemies, from small and fast, flying and
crawling, hard hitting and hard to hit.

Level design is pretty good. In the first half of the game every level is different and environments change each time. But later into the game levels become kinda samey. They're still fun to run and hack'n'slash through but it's not the same variety as in the first half of the game.

Graphically the game is a real eyecandy. Monsters, characters, especially in cut-scenes look stunning. Can't get enough of cut-scenes with Nico. Need more Nico. Please Capcom more Nico next game.
Environments on the other hand are not great. They still look good, nothing close to being ugly. I guess this is done to keep the performance good because it matters in a fast paced game. And speaking about performance it's great. The game ran at 90-100fps the whole time with no problems. Playing on 3440x1440 so a pretty high resolution on 7700k and 2070s. The performance is top notch.
Sadly no ultrawide support out of the box so you need to use a fix. After that the game runs flawlesly in ultrawide.

Sound design is done well too. Voice acting is great and soundtrack is amazing. Lots of good electronic and industrial tunes. Although I miss Combichrist.

Overall a great action game for casuals and hardcore fans. It may be easy it may be extremely challenging because of variety in difficulty settings so pretty much anyone into action games more or less should like it. Bad ass characters, over the top action and Nico makes this one of the best action games out there.

Pros
Each level feels fresh (for the most part)
Non-stop action
Good monster variety
Great character design
Did I mentioned Nico?
Soundrack
Amazing graphics
Could be challenging or extremely easy depending on your choice
Cons
Level variety is bland in the second half of the game

Follow my curator page for more

Smokin' Sexy Style!!
I fell in love with the game after watching the reveal trailer. When I finally got to play it, I wasn’t disappointed at all. Devil May Cry 5 is a very stylish hack and slash game. It’s got all what it needs: juicy action, badass music, top-notch graphics, and even a cool story with a few twists.

The visuals in the game are awesome. The characters look attractive, the enemies are highly detailed, and the animations are very smooth. The battles are pleasing not only to take part in but also to watch. I have a single concern about the design of the locations—they look a bit monotonous. Though, they still fit in the game. After all, the world is at the edge of the apocalypse, so it shouldn’t be pretty and colorful.


Devil May Cry 5 
A Screenshot of Devil May Cry 5
By: Red Queen

I can talk about the combat system forever. The variety of the combos is sure to keep you entertained. Dante has several fighting styles and weapons, Nero has various Devil Breakers, and V introduces the new pet system. Each of the characters has a unique playstyle that you’ll have to master to turn up the difficulty. The game will push you towards improving your skills. If you’re persistent enough, eventually you’ll be able to kill the most vicious demons at the highest difficulty while enjoying the SSS stylish rank.


Devil May Cry 5 
A Screenshot of Devil May Cry 5
By: Red Queen

The soundtrack is totally badass. The three character themes will get stuck in your head, whereas the other songs are not so catchy but still cool enough. As I’m a metal music fan, I really admired Subhuman.

The plot was never a forte of hack and slash games, yet in Devil May Cry 5 it’s quite exiting. You’ll definitely become a fond of it if you’re a DMC fan. In case you’ve never played any DMC games before, I recommend getting familiar with them first so that you can fully appreciate the story.


Devil May Cry 5 
A Screenshot of Devil May Cry 5
By: Red Queen

Devil May Cry 5 turned out to be a high-quality product. I enjoyed it all the way through. If you’re into hack and slash games, then Devil May Cry 5 wil certainly become one of your favorites.

Recommended
15.6 hrs on record
Posted: June 5, 2019
This is the only Devil May Cry game I’ve played besides DmC: Devil May Cry (that’s such a weird name. Devil May Cry x2?). I haven’t even completed DmC either. This is the only Devil May Cry game I’ve completed, and I loved every moment of it. I’m going to break it down and list the reasons what I disliked and liked about this game.

One of the first things I want to say is that I played this game with an Xbox One controller and only paid $20 for this. I may be biased, as I didn’t pay full price. However, I feel that it is worth that.

How does it look?
Devil May Cry 5 is one of the most beautiful games I’ve ever played. There’s so much detail done to every little thing that they put into this. You can tell the team was very passionate about what they were creating. The cutscenes were absolutely stunning and some of the most memorable cutscenes I’ve ever witnessed. There’s even an extra option to go back and watch the cutscenes. I did this several times just to look at how pretty and badass they were. Seeing Dante shred through demons, Nero using Red Queen and his new Devil Breakers, and V using his staff and companions to shatter enemies. It’s all very satisfying to watch and rewarding.

How does it sound?
This is the part where Devil May Cry 5 lost me. I know that several people that loved the soundtrack and several people that had the opposite opinions. Unfortunately, I’m one of those people. The soundtrack seems like it was made for children (this is my opinion). Some ambient music was great, but the theme songs for the characters (looking at you, Devil Trigger) took me out of the game. I just ended up having my own music in the background while I played. I’ve found that the soundtrack doesn’t really fit the game. It has more of an electronic/metal theme to it, but it’s just not as good as everything else this game offers. It usually just makes me laugh or cringe. Again, no offense to the people that liked it. Have a listen to the soundtrack for yourself on Spotify or YouTube. You may very well like it.

How does it play?
The Devil May Cry franchise has always been good about delivering a satisfying combat experience. The thing is, if you aren’t good with timing - you won’t have a good time. This game requires a little bit of skill, as things are about timing and setting yourself up for combos. Devil May Cry 5 gradually shows you how to do these pretty gradually and helps you get into the flow of what this game is. Once you get your preferred combos and weapons selected; this is where the game shines the brightest. Being able to lay into these demons and show them that you’re superior is one of the best feelings I’ve ever felt in a video game. If you love satisfying combos with a side of challenge, this game is perfect for you.

How is the story?
To be honest, I haven’t kept up with the Devil May Cry story. I didn’t know who all of these people were when I started playing. However, it did a great job of letting me know who was who and why they were so significant. I’ve grown to care about all of the characters and learn about who they were and what their motivations were. Devil May Cry 5 does a great job with character dialogue and interaction. Seeing these characters talk and fight seems pretty realistic and is often really cool. Seeing the characters react to their emotions and see how they actually feel is really refreshing.

Overall...
I highly recommend this game, even if you don’t typically like 3rd person games. Capcom knew what Devil May Cry 5 needed to offer, and they perfected it. Beautiful visuals, satisfying combat, and an amazing story. Please pick up this game whenever you can afford it. You won’t regret it.

I'm really tired of having to deal with the DENUVO ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥, therefore, I'm not going to recommend DMC5 on PC. Don't get me wrong, the game is amazing, probably the best DMC game of them all (I'm serious), but the ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ that Capcom has pulled off with DENUVO on PC it's just too much.

Capcom released this game by mistake with a DENUVO-less exe, then, released a patch to put DENUVO back in. That allowed people to notice how the game ran faster, better, without FPS drops, lag, stutter and much faster loading times without DENUVO.

I don't support piracy but DRM is not the solution. You only need one example to understand this: CD Projekt RED. Hard work, dedication, costumer respect and releasing quality products is what fights piracy.

Pirates are playing this game for free while us, the legit costumers, have to deal with online checks while we play that eat up CPU power, increasing loading times and generating FPS drops.

So no, I don't recommend DMC5 on PC, despite being the best DMC game ever.

Devil May Cry 5 is a stellar return to form for the series, capitalizing on all the elements that make it great. Charismatic characters and stylish, over-the-top fighting mix together into an experience that keeps you hooked to your seat for the initial 15+ hours, and possibly more as you delve into higher difficulties. Mick
200 products in account
0
44 people found this review helpful
4 people found this review funny 0

Recommended
25.4 hrs on record
Posted: September 15, 2019
I waited 10 years to play this game. The last DMC game from Capcom was in 2008.
And starting the game, holding your gamepad, and just loading into the title screen made me scream like a kid.

Lets start off with some basics that Capcom or DMC series never fails to impress me:

+ Combat - Yup, this is it, the pinnacle of hack and slash , all at the same time making your characters COOL AF while performing them. If you're an anime fan, you'll be right in the shoes of your power fantasy. The combat system is quite hard to get used to, at first and a lot harder to master, so pulling off those sick moves will make you grin like the grim reaper. But wait, there's also an "Auto" mode that enables complex combos to be chained with the press of buttons, if you're interested in an easier gameplay, but you lose the finer control on chaining the right combos.

Nero : The moves are so fluid, every time i played Nero, i paused each move just to see that they didnt even cut corners in the animations. Nero's devilbringers, ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥.... to see the intricate details of an arm that's mostly not even visible when in combat, is just amazing. You can see all the animations for each arm being unique and right, The gameplay mechanics integrated into that arm alone kept me just trying them out in open spaces again and again. The sword and gun play is as expected from Nero, Smooth and consistent, you never are afraid when being surrounded by enemies. They went overkill with the eXceed mechanic with a certain devil bringer, the red queen glows in fiery red exhausting flames and there's visible heatwaves surrounding it. Also, Nero is still cheesy and cringe-worthy as usual.

V : Playing V is the power fantasy of those that love the master-minion theme. Dude has the charisma of Daila Lama and the edgy attitude of an anime villain. You stand far back, you let your demonic pets do your job and they equate to a snarky hawk that spews electricity and a silent shapeshifting panther that can turn into any weapon that kills, then there's a giant golem that he can summon that fires death beams, so yea. Playing V is like conducting an orchestra, You press buttons, and the right buttons at the right time makes death rain on your foes. Just a joy as most hack and slash games have never had such an implementation where the character himself isn't involved as much. Again brilliant gameplay and character design, oh and did i mention, he READS A BOOK WHILE IN BATTLE to charge his ultimate?! His alluring charm also attracts all weebs to rise up and say "Yare Yare Daze".

Dante : Yo, this is the OG in my heart when it comes to hack'n'slash games. As we've all grown(DMC fans), Every adult has wanted a game character that not only is super strong and powerful, always saving the world and etc, but also at times weak, vulnerable , desperate and the raw desire to claim the "COOL AF" title and Dante is it. This mofo is the jack of all demonic trades, his controls,weapon sets, combo moves are some of the best in the FREAKING GAMING INDUSTRY. It was a sheer adrenaline rush every time you started combat with Dante. Capcom made a motorcycle into a freaking dual chainsaw, If you people remember your favorite weapons from DMC 3 and 4, well Spolier alert: . Overall 10 years of wait was totally satisfied when controlling this badass mofo. Every weapon mechanic while in combat is the extension of Dante's attitude which is an amazing feeling to capture and portray to players, so kudos Capcom.

+ Character Design - All the characters in the game are so well designed especially now that the game uses RE6, everything looks so much better. Even though the game will ride off its combat loop more, characters are still flushed out especially for a hack and slash game. Enemy and boss design are cool, but you wont be noticing them when you're launching them into the stratosphere and due to fast pace of each encounter.

+ World Design - Capcom isn't new to this world ending scenario nor are they not aware of how level designs work for hack and slash games. Tight linear areas with room to show off your moves, nothing complex and keeping you progress forward. Although this is first DMC that has been generous with the red orbs, its almost everywhere. RE6 engine provides nice backdrops and everything feels as expected.

+ Story - Well, as a fanboy and someone whose been playing all the DMC games till now, it was quite satisfying but not exhilarating to be honest, but quite satisfying is a high note for these type of games. First time players would be more disappointed as they would not feel the same connection to the storyline or characters. Imagine watching a soap opera from Season 3 instead of 1, You'll enjoy it but you wont get the full picture. There is a short reminder of the events of DMC in game, so that could help.

So for DMC fans, this game is a must play and most you would have pre-ordered just like me. And for the newer players, its an experience you rarely find in the gaming industry, a fun and thrilling roller coaster ride that can reduce your irl stress by button smashing(or calculating moves) and looking cool at the same time. You will not be disappointed. I hope this review was a good read.

Final Verdict:

11/10 for combat and 8/10 for Story = 9/10 for the game.

Edit:
forgot to add my budget specs: i5 4440, GTX 1060 6GB and 16 GB RAM. Game ran locked on max settings 60fps@1080p. And if you're wondering about the hours shown, i finished it on console and replaying it on PC. It takes about 20 hrs to complete the story and even more if your doing everything besides just the story.

Well well well, the Vergil DLC is here.

Vergil :
The alpha and omega of the series, it is truly a marvel seeing Vergil dominate the battlefield with such finesse. The weapons and moves reflect this ideology that less is more and calm is deadly. If anyone has played DMC4, this will feel like putting on familiar gloves in terms on control.
So every time I did some flashy moves or used DT on vergil, I recorded my gameplay, viewed it in half the playback speed and the details are all there. Just beautiful. A reminder that the new dlc isn't something of a new story, it's more of the same story with some added stuff here and there.

Sure you might not have raytracing (yet?), but Turbo Mode and Legendary Dark Knight are 100% possible, not to mention the plethora of gameplay adjustments and fixes available from the modding community to customize the game to fit your playstyle and your aesthetic.

Did I mention there's also a functioning online co-op mod? Yes, said mod is janky and needs the stars to align to work cause Capcom didn't account for the networking system to be used this way at all, but when it works it's some of the most dumb fun I've had with any game in ages. Also they just figured out how to get co-op LDK to work and it's crazy as all butt.

What I'm trying to get across here is that it's frustrating that Capcom has the power to support this game in many ways imaginable but choose not to. I get why the PS4 and Xbox One can't get updated with most of Special Edition's new additions, but not PC? Really now? It sucks that we have to rely on modding for some of those features, but honestly it's still impressive as all hell that the community loves this game enough to make all this cool stuff for us to try out that you can't get anywhere else.

Seriously, I loved the base game as is, but modding it has changed it into some life-changing ♥♥♥♥. I've put in 45+ more hours into this version of the game since modding it and I plan to put in much more until I somehow get bored. I don't wanna be all "durrrrr fans do what Capcom don't", and I'm not trying to be, but I just want to say that the DMC community has the power to put out some amazing work that increases the longevity of these games tenfold, so if you love DMC and want to break the limits on its already amazing gameplay, I highly suggest looking into all the cool additions and adjustment some modders out there are working on, it's truly incredible stuff.
 

marcos!

If you are someone who as a kid, was watching early 2000's action movies like Matrix trilogy or Blade trilogy, and dreamed to play a game that would let you feel like main protagonist of films mentioned above, then look no further - this is something for you.

Just grab it when you can, it's THAT good. Deluxe edition recommended for DMC fans.

5 star gamer
87 products in account
0
30 people found this review helpful
2 people found this review funny 0

Recommended
21.5 hrs on record
Posted: March 19, 2019
I'll be honest, the only DMC title I'd played prior to this one was the reboot, and I've been completely blown out of the water by how much of a jump in quality DMC5 has been compared to that. It may not be devoid of problems, but few games are, and if someone asked me for a standout example of a character action game I'd point to this without hesitation.

The Gameplay

Controls are responsive and incredibly easy to learn, even on M/KB, so players both old and new to action games will be able to quickly get a handle on using their full moveset. Though you have a ton of actions at your disposal, they're carefully introduced over the course of the first few levels, helping the integration of each into your tactics remain smooth. In lieu of a light/heavy attack system, the buttons are instead divided by melee/ranged/special, with directional inputs, button holds, or mid-combo delays being how you perform various moves. This system let them pack a ton of moves into each weapon without an excess of buttons, but it hits a bit of a snag should the camera ever decide to turn unexpectedly. While a move's input may be listed as W + Left Click while locked on, what it -actually- means is press whatever direction is towards the enemy you're locked on to. As a result, if you knock a foe around and the camera turns to keep them in view, all of the directional inputs are shifted, and it can be quite awkward to try to adjust to this mid-combo.

Movesets sport a ton of variety, letting you constantly mix up your attacks and ensuring there's never a dull or spammy moment during combat (if you're Dante or Nero, at least). Dante has 4 weapons for both ranged and melee, each of which have incredibly fun designs (you can beat people to death by swinging around a motorcycle or throwing a hat around like Michael Jackson), and adds to that with 4 combat styles he can switch between that add extra actions to his arsenal. You can swap weapons and styles mid-combo, allowing for some downright astounding combos. Nero sticks to a single sword and gun, which sport a solid moveset by themselves, but the real meat of his variation comes from the 8 cybernetic arms that make up his 3rd attack button. From lightning punches, performing grabs ala DMC4, or firing out a flying rocket arm, he gets a ton of variety from these, and can eventually equip all 8 at once (or multiples of the same, as they can be broken by using supers or getting hit mid-attack). In an odd design decision, you can't switch arms mid-level, instead needing to destroy your current one to equip the next one, but at the very least this encourages you to make use of their super moves.

Sadly, V doesn't hold up nearly as well as our other heroes. Though he gets a solid deal of move variation through his three demon pets (a bird for ranged attacks, a shapeshifting panther for melee, and a giant laser-spewing golem for super moves), it still amounts to significantly less than the other characters. On top of this, the panther and golem both suffer from downright clunky AI. It's not uncommon to lock onto an enemy and summon your panther, only for him to appear 20ft in front of your target and just swing wildly at the air, wasting your time and killing your combo rating. The golem (and the other demons, if you spend meter to put them on autopilot) likewise has a tendency to wait a long time between attacks, wasting chunks of your super meter on nothing. He's even worse should you decide to take manual control, handling like a drunken sloth. V's moveset has a really cool design with a lot of potential behind it, so it's a shame it ended up such a clunky mess.

Balance & Enemy Design

DMC5 is in an awkward place with its balance. On the one hand, getting an S-rank for any given mission is genuinely challenging, and it's a ton of fun to push yourself to achieve that. Regular enemies have plenty of variety, and on NG+ are used in some really neat combinations. Bosses are solid final challenges to their levels, and their movesets even get expanded if you play on NG+ to really push you to your limit. It's awkward because DMC5 uses an unconventional setup of the first playthrough being "training" for the "real" experience in NG+. This works pretty good as long as you're the type who digs multiple runs, as the enemy placement on NG+ is so drastically different that you're practically playing different levels with the same story, but one-and-done types may find the regular fights lacklustre as a result, as there's multiple enemy types that only appear 2-3 times on the first playthrough, and even some of the weaker types end up underused.

Also there's the gold orb system; extra lives that revive you on the spot with no progress lost. You get a veritable pile of them throughout the game (I'd earned 25 or so by the end), and can also use regular upgrade currency, and as a result you can power through any difficult encounter by just reviving. While this won't impact people going for S-ranks, as using a revive tanks 25% of your score, people just concerned with beating every level may find their challenge being hampered quite a bit when they realize their death is nigh-meaningless.

As mentioned, the enemies have some incredible variety. You'll be up against a great deal of creative mechanics, such as a huge alligator-thing who can be freed from a muzzle to allow it to deal friendly fire to other enemies in exchange for increasing its range and attack power, cleaver-wielding berserkers who temporarily gain stun immunity and new attacks after being knocked down, or firebats who try to self-destruct if their HP gets low. Even the fodder enemy types have at least 3-4 attacks, so even minor combat encounters stay interesting.

Most bosses have a huge variety of attacks, and are each incredibly fun fights in their own right, though at least a couple suffer from having an attack that moves them really far away from you, messing with the flow of combat a bit. Also, a couple bosses are just introductory fights for regular enemies, and one mission is just fighting a big walker who only has two attacks and way too much HP. Mind you most of the bosses are still really fun, but 20% of your bosses being doody is a noteworthy percentage.

The Story

It's campy, cheesy, and wonderfully over-the-top. The characters may be vaguely American, but the tale they're involved in is as anime as it gets, and it's fantastic. It mixes the serious plot bits and the sassy snark together in a way that isn't awkward, something plenty of games try and fail at doing. If you've never played a DMC game before, there's an optional recap cutscene, and given that this was my first real DMC I'd say people unfamiliar with the series will still enjoy it a great deal.

The Graphics and Sound

The RE Engine remains a juggernaut of good looks. The human characters look great, and the enemies are straight-up menacing. The city supplements its standard bombed-out look with massive demonic tree roots and the creepy husks of blood-drained victims, and the levels inside of the giant underworldly tree are sometimes downright beautiful in a weird, hellish sort of way.

I found some of the brosteppy or screamo-y regular battle tracks in this very grating, but it ended up winning me over with the solid mix of rock and electronic in the boss tracks. The script has some lines that read a bit awkwardly, but the voice cast are all so solid that they more than make up for it.

In Closing

If you're a DMC fan, I've no doubt you'll love this entry, especially after the reboot. If you're a character action fan in general, then while this has some clunky spots, it's still a very welcome addition to the genre, and anyone who wants a solid challenge should enjoy it a great deal.

8.7/10

Check out my Curator for even more reviews, including stuff I ghost-write through Family Share!

49.8 hrs on record
Posted: April 2, 2019
I won’t lie, Devil May Cry 5 had me hesitant. From the moment they announced micro-transactions for currency in a single player game I was highly sceptical of what scummy business-model Capcom may try and leverage into the game. Was it going to be insanely grindy? Could they make the best weapons hidden behind pay-walls and therefore enforce a ‘fun tax’?

To be blunt, I didn’t trust it.

Then the game came out and it had fantastic reception. This turned my head and got me curious. I looked into it and it appears for the most part my concerns are unfounded.

The game did let you buy its main currency, and it looked like a few weapons were locked behind a pay-walls, but for the most part these looked like fun little gimmicks (a Megaman blaster arm for example) rather than any kind of major content. and there was only really one minor skill for each character that I would say was overpriced in an attempt to sell red orb DLC.

I was interested, but I still couldn’t quite bring myself to buy the game.

Then I had the chance to meet two of the games lead creators, Hideaki Itsuno and Matt Walker at Sydney Madfest 2019. They were fantastic, cool and fun guys and they managed to get me hype enough that when I got home I straight away bought Devil May Cry 5.

The game has been an absolute blast. Personally, it is my favourite entry in the entire franchise. Each of the three character play in there own way that is super fluid, unique and fun. It took me a couple of hours to wrap my head around the new character V (thought a lot of this is because my console controller is held together with nothing but tape and the hopes and dreams of my perpetually empty wallet). But once I did I was getting those SSS ranks no problem.

Nero’s play style feels like an evolution of his character in Devil May Cry 4, particularly after the first playthrough, when you have access to all his different powers and skills.

Finally, Dante plays like Dante, because why mess with perfection? He gets a whole bunch of cool new weapons and some old favourites re-imagined (I don’t want to spoil too much, but lets just say Kalina Ann has a sister, and you get to play with them both).

If you want a more in depth look at the play style I suggest looking at direct gameplay footage. If I try to explain though words it will just sound clumsy and dumb.

Now I want to take a look at the plot for a brief moment.

It works fine. I know some people really get into the stories of these games, and to that I say more power to you. Personally, I’ve always found they are little bit too predictable and bland, so besides that little teenage edge-lord voice that giggles with glee at every biblical or Divine Comedy reference, all I can really say is that it does its job and it does it well enough. Characters, setting and motivations are all established and presented in (with the exception of a few RE Engine uncanny-valley demon faces) beautifully rendered cut scenes.

If I did have one criticism of the narrative, it would be that this is a story of Dante, Nero and V. I love each of these boys. Then there is Nico, who serves as an engineer, building new gear for Nero (I know she has a few haters out there but I like her well enough) which gives her a direct impact in the plot. However, then Trish and Lady are there… Because? I don’t want to hate on Trish and Lady, they are both great. But I feel like they are there to placate the fanbase. Mainly to assure them that this isn’t another Ninja Theory spin-off title, rather than for any actual narrative or gameplay contribution.

All I’m saying is I want the girls out there doing what they do best: wreaking house and killing demons. Make that DLC campaign happen Capcom!

Devil May Cry 5 is the greatest scratch to my inner edge-lord itch since the first Matrix movie. I can highly recommend it to anyone who is into character action games.

Finally I just wanted to say this game claims to have multiplayer. Just a warning, it doesn’t in any meaningful sense. Google it if you want to understand the specifics. You won’t so much ‘play with your friends’ as ‘exist vaguely in the same space as randoms’.

9.8/10. Literally one of the best games I've ever played. Phenomenal story & incredible graphics/gameplay.

Combat:- DMC is known for being a hack and slash and that's exactly what they've done. The combat in this game once again is brilliant. It runs smoothly, each new unlock is soothing and enjoyable to use & the variety of multiple combo's/attacks/death animations that you can witness throughout playing this will leave you entertained for hours. Definitely a great deal of attention was put into creating this game and it really does pay off.

Graphics:- The graphics and detail put into every single mission, facial structure & enemy is beyond amazing. I expected a great amount of detail already but each new enemy/scenic setting/character & boss just left me amazed at the beautiful amount of time they've spent on each and every single thing.

Bosses:- Quite easy on the standard difficulties but I can imagine them being rather brutal the harder the difficulty gets. Really enjoyable and extremely fun to kill each boss/mini-boss in this game. Especially the main opposition that you're trying to kill.

Humour:- I was worried when I witnessed some humour at the start of the game and didn't want this to become a "meme" story whatsoever but by the end of the game I easily noted to myself that every single ounce of humour/joke amongst the game was PERFECTLY placed and fit in place just right. Especially towards the ending of the game & that dance scene? oh boy...that was hilarious. (You'll know when you get to it)

Story/Lore:- Absolutely superb. I was confused at times & definitely worried that I was going to have a quick fight with a boss and that would be the end of the game when I felt I was near the end but I have never been so wrong in my life. The "ending" was at least 4-5 missions and lasted just under two hours of gameplay I'd say. It's not just one boss fight, it's multiple fights, story linking together, lore and pieces combining and making sense. You learn SO much and you truly appreciate everything this game became. Not to mention everything else above...wow.

I've not been this blown away in a very long time with a game. a MUST buy. Especially if you get a discount. ~12 hours of gameplay to complete which is the reason this isn't a 10/10. Otherwise, truly breathtaking.

63.1 hrs on record
Posted: January 9, 2020
Well, the Resident Evil 2 remake was really good and I played it a lot. So when starting this game I had pretty high expectations. Let's say I wasn't disappointed.

Apart from the occasional samey level design (looking at you missions 14 to 16) and some pretty 'spongy' enemies at higher difficulties, this game is really well made. The graphics, music and art style are all spot on. The ending is a bit too cliff-hanger for my taste, but that doesn't make the game any less fun to play.

The three characters all feature unique abilities and techniques that require some solid investment to flesh out fully, but you really want to look at the missions again to find more fragments, secret missions and hidden spots plus challenging yourself to face the enemies at a higher difficulty that it doesn't become tedious. The game play is almost always on point and figuring out how to get a higher combat rating while trying your acquired combos and skills is a lot of fun.

A very solid action game that adds a lot of replay value and an interesting set of playable characters. I'd recommend getting the game if you like fast paced action games that are challenging, but not frustrating.

Recommended
51.7 hrs on record
Posted: March 16, 2019
+Pros:

+The game was more difficult than I expected. Higher difficulties add more moves to bosses and enemies and make them smarter and more aggressive and not just give them higher numbers.

+The Soundtrack is spot on! Every character has their own battle theme and they all fit perfectly, Especially Nero's battle theme (Devil Trigger). Every boss fight has a theme too continuing the series style

+Levels are not a bit more open and have diverging paths/secret paths which adds to the games replayability.

+Enemy designs are great and rivals the best in the series, 3. Maybe even surpasses it but only time will tell. It has some enemies from past games with new moves and a bunch of new enemies. All of which are fun to fight against and none are annoying, except for Fury.

+Boss fights are nice. They range from good to great.

+The Gameplay is this game's strong point. Maybe not as deep as 4 though. Dante's new weapons are a blast to play around with, and Nero's new devil breakers are extremely unique feeling and will make you want to play him even more.

+Some missions are playable with multiple characters which, Most of the time go in different routes so you will get to explore new places once you replay the game with the other characters you didn't pick at the time.

+Secret Missions are near perfect, They are the right amount of secret, and most of them are the right amount of difficult. you won't get all of them in the first playthough so you'll want to go back and play it again so you can find them.

+Blue orb & Purple orb fragments are well hidden in the level but are still possible to find.

+A notable feature in the settings is the adjustable camera length. This is an amazing feature that I wish more games would do.

+Another notable feature is the timeline between the mission loading screens, It has the date and time of day in which the mission you are about to go into is happening and where it fits in the overall timeline of the game.


-Cons:

-A lot of the settings don't really affect the game, just the cut-scenes. People want to turn off certain things so they can get a better frame rate while playing not in a cut-scene.

-Game lacks hard mode from the beginning. You need to play Normal difficulty first to unlock it. Also Legendary Dark Knight difficulty is not present in the game. It was very enjoyable in 4.

- Lady's voice acting is bad. Not really bad, just bad. Definitely the worst in the game.

- Trish's face model looks so ugly. It's just so bad. I don't know how it got through the final game.

- Since CAPCOM did the voice acting and the motion capture separate. Lip sync issues occur a lot in the game.

-Occasional cringe worthy lines.

-Environments lack diversity and can really mush together which is weird since this is something 4 got so well.

-Like every other DMC there is a boss rush mission. Although it is better in some aspects it's worse in others. It limits your abilities per boss fight and is utterly a bad design choice that, depending on your choice of boss in the beggining can somewhat break the gameplay.

-The game lacks turbo mode which made everything run faster in-game. I always played the games this way and playing 5 without it feels like a slog. I downloaded a mod to fix this.

-V is a bore to play with. Since V isn't the one fighting, the game tries to teleport them near enemies or near you when it thinks you need it. And most of the time it works and when it does you don't even notice it but sometimes it doesn't and you notice it hard. They would just teleport to you while you were doing a certain combo and now everything is ruined. He is also very slow and lacks the combo possibilities of the other.


-We should have been allowed to pick any character in any mission after beating the game to fight the different bosses with different characters.

-No Skins. We could have gotten skins from DMC 1-2-3-4 and coatless variations. Maybe even more Skins that didn't make the cut. Ultimately CAPCOM chose the lazy approach and just changed colours and called them skins.

-Micro-transactions. The game has buyable reb orbs, and although I'm 1000% against it, It really doesn't affect the game so I won't say they do, but would rather them not be in the game. What are bad micro-transactions though are the 4 extra devil breakers for Nero and the alt variation of the bike for Dante that has a stinger move in the air. To have moves locked behind a paywall in an action game like DMC is comparable to pay to win.

- Nero's new devil breakers aren't unlocked clearly. Only 2 of them have the same moves as their respective bosses and are unlocked after them. Other than that the rest are just unlocked after a boss and have no correlation with that specific boss. Would have been better if they were like the weapons.

-Low amount of humanoid bosses where can you have a 1v1. Also most bosses lack personality.

-Game lacks puzzles and overall metroid-vania design of 1 and 3, Which just makes you breeze through the environment and not really interact with it most of the time.

- No ability, after beating the game, to pick devil breakers for nero and no ability to switch between them without breaking them.

TL;DR:


To say Devil May Cry 5 wasn't a disappointment for me would be a lie. A lot of things that are known in the series are missing in 5, And the game lacks innovation, I thought they could make a lot more things with the formula that would have taken the game to another level. But in the end I'm just glad DMC is back with a solid entry and I hope it's not the last one since I can still see a lot of potential in the series.
