Grim Piñata
203 products in account
4
30 people found this review helpful
2 people found this review funny 2

Recommended
18.8 hrs on record
Posted: May 29, 2021
Devil May Cry 5 is easily the most accessible game in the series for new players, while still offering all the series staples that existing fans love. I highly recommend picking it up when you can as the combat is stylish, environments and character models look great, the playable roster has been expanded and the soundtrack is amazing.

Story
In a first for the series DMC5 actually offers a quick history of series, listing each game in chronological order that can be viewed from the main menu. While it’s might not interest existing fans, it really helps new players understand who everyone is and saves you from having to flounder around trying to figure out why should care about any of the characters. I thought the story was impressive and well-paced with each chapter slowly revealing new information while following each of the 3 main characters journeys, with it being a race against time before events spiral out of hand. There seems to be a lot more humour in DMC5, especially between the main cast and Nico (the mechanic/ arms dealer). Dante’s flamboyant (arsehole) attitude seems to have been toned right down compared to DMC3 (I no longer want to throw a controller through the screen every time he speaks), and Nero (from DMC4) returns as still being hot-headed but learning to control his rashness. V acts a mysterious foil against both of the others, with a calm and matter of fact attitude, though his demon summon griffon makes up for it with attitude. While the story sort of ends with battles that you expect from the series, the path to them does take a few unexpected twists, and is quite enjoyable.

Gameplay
Gameplay is the same as previous games, you fight in enclosed combat spaces and use different combinations of moves to increase the rank gauge and try not to get hit (which resets the score). Higher combat scores provide better rewards, which allow you to purchase more moves and upgrade existing ones. The games overall difficulty is easier than past entries until you start unlocking the other modes which increase the difficulty to stupid levels (hell and hell being the choice for masochists). It also offers an option of auto enabling moves (like auto charging weapons), switching fight modes(Dante) and helping to chain attacks which makes combat much easier, but reduces your rewards.

Combat is vastly different depending on which character you are playing. Dante relies on different combat styles to change damage and moves set, while also wielding some outrageous weapons (if you ever wanted to wield a motorcycle as a sword this game has you covered). Nero has sword techniques, but his gimmick has him making use of disposable combat arms that each provide different effects and can be charged up for a one use super move (every wanted to see what mega man’s buster arm would look like on a person- you now can). V doesn’t attack at all, relying on his 3 summoned demons to attack (with him doing the final attack to kill them). The demons can be damaged (and can’t attack when damaged too much until they recover). I found V easiest to play with, but with auto assist it just becomes a button mashing exercise as long as you remember to move around so V doesn’t get hit.

There seems to be a lot less emphasis on puzzles, with there being more focus on combat, exploration of the environment, and boss fights. Exploring does prove to be worthwhile, as there are plenty of upgrade orbs hidden around stages, as well as other items to use, and secret missions to complete for rewards. There is a fair amount to do post game, from playing on each of the 6 different difficulties (they each unlock other modes, available upgrades or costumes), taking pictures of enemies dying (yes this is a thing), and completing the bloody palace, a 101 floor timed battle against different waves of enemies and bosses that can be completed with each of the characters. There is also a minimal online mode, where you are in the same stage as others (your progress doesn’t affect them in any way), where you can rate each other’s performance and award golden orbs.

Graphics
DMC5 has to be the best looking game in the series. While there aren’t many different locales (ruined city, inside a hell plant and hell itself) all look really good and is highly detailed (you see blood pumping through plants, walls look slimy). The environments don’t seem as dark as in DMC3 and collectables aren’t hidden in areas you can barely see. There is plenty of destructible object in the environment, however the environment itself seems immune to damage apart from superficial textures changes. Each characters are animated really well, and equipped weapons and items are always showed on characters when used in cut scenes. There is even an option to replace all the animated cut scenes with real actors in the menu (you can see these later in the gallery, but they are worth watching). I didn’t experience any crashes or screen tearing, and there was very little clipping. Sone of the mob enemies return from previous games, however none of them are recycled in DMC5 (you don’t encounter different variants that are just a colour swap). I thought all of the bosses were very good, and while they all test your ability to figure out attack patterns I thought the fight through the city was a standout (even if the fight itself is easy).

Music
The DMC series is known for its good music (and the heavy metal that plays when Dante is fighting), and DMC 5 doesn’t disappoint. Each character has different battle tracks when they fight (some are quite subtle compared to Dante’s standard battle music with a lot less screaming), but all increase in energy as your fighting rank increases (it’s not an increase in tempo, but choruses get added, and the songs change). It’s a very cool way to reward the player when they are performing well in combat (rather than just throwing extra experience at the player). All of the voice acting is excellent, and the effort has gone into making the character animation match the vocals. The script is very well written, I didn’t notice any overly cringey speeches, and the banter between the characters is a lot funnier (Dante seems to have mellowed in his old age).

DLC
There is an absolute ton of DLC options, with majority of it falling under boosting or cosmetic options. These can be handy if you aren’t going to play more than once, and want to use the best moves or different outfits, but majority of the moves will be unlocked after one playthrough. Some of the other DLC options are much more interesting, with Vergil being a playable character as well as the battle tracks from previous games being available to use in fights. Vergil has a different move sets, combos, however doesn’t add anything to the story (this is pure fan service).

Achievements
If you are chasing 100% achievements, then getting S ranks on Hell on Hell mode will likely see most people give up. Congratulation if you pull it off, as it requires complete mastery and knowledge of move sets, enemies and boss fights and requires perfect dodging. You also need to purchase the Virgil DLC.

For more reviews please visit https://store.steampowered.com/curator/31327216/

Mister Dante

Recommended
50.9 hrs on record
Posted: December 4, 2021
TL;DR: A ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ BLAST to play. 10/10 for me. I'd totally recommend it to anyone.

A nice thing about this game (at least in my opinion) is you can decide if this game is for you by watching the Intro credit cinematic, if you don’t like that cinematic, you won’t understand what DMC is and this game and franchise is not for you. But anyway, moving on, in terms of story itself, I really liked it. Even though it’s definitely not the best stories or anything. It’s a mediocre story with predictable events for the most part. If you wanna buy this game for just it’s story and if you aren’t a DMC fan, then you probably won’t like it. But a nice thing that this game does have is a “History of DMC” option for new players to understand a bit about the universe so you’re not really going into DMC 5’s story blind. Either way, the story is 4/5 I’d say. (I’m a bit biased on the story, so if I’m being honest, it would be a 3/5 or something, an average story)

BUT the gameplay…. The gameplay literally carries this game’s review to 10/10 in my opinion. I’ll go one by one on character gameplay review. But I’ll say this before I go there, the soundtracks for each character, especially Nero’s...is soooo good. Casey Edwards has done SO MUCH for this game by just his music.

V:
Okay, this character’s gameplay…. might get boring depending on your taste. He’s kind of a zoner in a hack and slash game, which actually is a unique idea for a hack and slash. And I’m glad they experimented with this. V is by no means bad though, but once you start enjoying the game for what it really is, you’ll understand what I’m talking about.
But Nero and Dante…. boy oh boy!

Nero:
I was already a fan of Nero from 4 even though fans didn’t really like Nero much apparently. But in this game, the feature of “Devil Breakers” (a major part of Nero’s kit in gameplay) is the best thing the devs decided to do for this game. And this in my opinion raises Nero’s combo potentials SO high….my god. I LOVE playing Nero as much as Dante. I’m by no means a master of this series or combat, but his gameplay is so satisfying. He certainly has earned his spot in this franchise with this game.

Dante:
What’s not to like about Dante? He’s badass as usual. And the addition of a few weapons in this game makes him even more fun. Like I previously said, I’m no master in this game and I’m trying to learn everything while I play. I’ve only kinda mastered the “Swordsman” style so far. But combining all his styles in gameplay is what makes him really really fun to play.

Vergil:
OMG, WHY ARE YOU SO MUCH FUN TO PLAY? You thought Nero and Dante was fun? Try Vergil and you won't touch those two for a while. He makes you feel so overpowered and makes you get into his edgy character while you play as him too. Even while making you feel op, he's so balanced. Capcom, sincerely hats off to you on this game. His gameplay combined with his track "Bury the Light", holy moly.......You can't just stop killing.

Enough about gameplay though. Even if you finish this game, it’ll still leave you wanting for more. I legit wanna try doing a 100% achievement or close to that for this game. The replay potential for this game is so nice. The bloody palace is a great way for you to keep playing the game. And if you wanna challenge yourself in story, there’s higher difficulties there as well. Although I’ve heard it gets boring in higher difficulties in story due to how much health the mobs and the bosses have. So, just settle with the “Son of Sparda” difficulty, which is the perfect difficulty according to a lot of players (including me). The voice acting is amazing and a HUGE part of this game. The cinematics, the world, I was immersed as hell while playing this game. Holy hell this was a blast to play. So, I’ll end my review here by saying this game is DEFINITELY worth it if you wanna pick it up on sale (full price is a bit too much to ask in my opinion tbh) and if you’re interested in hack and slash even by a little. Even if you’re not, who knows? Maybe you’ll end up loving it regardless.

Oh my god

I've never had this much fun in a videogame in like, years.

The adrenaline really gets you going with it's awesome soundtrack, pulling off a perfect royal guard as Dante and then hearing SS Rank kick in, it really feels out of this world.

The story is amazing, their is a lot of throwbacks to DMC3 and it welcomes new and old players to the fifth installment in a really good way, the characters are super memorable and really shine throughout the game.

The gameplay is nicely fleshed out as the entire campaign is split up between 3 characters, you've got Dante for going over the top with weapons, Nero for more smooth gameplay with minimal switching, and V for strategy (controlling more than 1 character) it's all preference on who you like the most as some missions let you choose who you want to play.

Multiple playthroughs of the game are rewarding (Super players after DMD) and has quite a lot of replayability in gamemodes such as Bloody Palace and in higher difficulties like Heaven or Hell. (HOH pretty much turns it into a shooter when you one shot everything.)

Would I recommend this?
Well, I didn't play a lot of action games before this but Devil May Cry 5 100% changed my perspective on them, BUY it if you love action and fast paced gameplay.

I personally think it's GOTY 2019 for Action, that's how much I liked it.

Why didn't I play any of the older games before ? I always heard that Devil May Cry was kind of a joke in the gaming community with the games being too anime, over the top, difficult and apparently some of the ones before this, pretty bad. But this game...... this game........ it is amazing. It is still anime as hell, over the top, difficult (especially if you're new) but most definitely not bad. Easy to pick up and play for all types of people. Great job capcom, I hope you revamp all of your franchises in the same way.

Quilliano
6,980 products in account
0
15 people found this review helpful 0

Recommended
7.9 hrs on record
Posted: April 4, 2019
If you enjoy this review please consider following my Curator page here .


I’ve always enjoyed character action games or spectacle fighters, whatever you want to call them, with the Bayonetta games, Metal Gear Rising and yes, DmC. I know that DmC gets quite a bad rap within the Devil May Cry community, but I frankly loved it. Perhaps this was due to the fact that I have only dabbled in the mainline series with the first DMC on PS2 as well as DMC 4, both of which I bounced off of pretty hard. Well I’m happy to say that this was not the case with DMC V. It’s great.

First off, the game offers a great recap of the previous games for those like myself, who never played through the earlier games. It set the table well and I felt as if I more or less knew who everyone was and what their motivations were. Although the story here isn’t main attraction. While I found the story to filled with melodrama and be over the top while still remaining somewhat self-aware, people play these for the tight gameplay.

Perhaps more so than any other character action game I’ve played, DMC V feels almost like a traditional fighting game, with precise button prompts and a deep suite of combos. For those who are not as dexterous or want all the flash without necessarily having to remember combos, there is an ‘Auto’ setting where you can still perform all of the fancy, high level combos without as much fuss. I found this to be a great way to empower the player and give them flexibility with choice. Of the main characters, Dante was my favorite, no surprise there. What I was surprised at though is how much I enjoyed playing as V compared to Nero. V has essentially no physical attacks, instead using avatars to fight for him. I found this be compelling in that it was such a departure from what you normally see in these types of games and I found it to be a bold design choice that paid off.

Graphically, the game looks fantastic. I had it nearly maxed out at 1440p on a 1060 and it held a rock-steady 60fps at all times. Capcom’s new RE Engine seems to be optimised exceptionally well and I imagine will scale very nicely. I would say that my main gripe with the game is that I found the levels to be pretty uninspired. There’s a lack of distinctive and memorable areas, instead we get a lot of crumbled buildings and bloody, pulsating masses. Now I know given the context these themes suite the game, I just wish there would have been a bit more creativity on the level design front.

Overall, Devil May Cry V is an excellent action game for newcomers like myself and I’m confident veterans will enjoy it too. Whether you want to use ‘Auto Combo’ to pull of flawless flashy combos or you want to hone your skills mastering and memorizing movesets, there’s something here for everyone.
 

ParanoidAndroid
802 products in account
0
22 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 0

Recommended
15.9 hrs on record
Posted: January 27, 2020
I don't usually play third-person action games with the exception of From Software whose works I have followed for a long time. After seeing how this game had beaten out fan favorites and big names for Action Game of the Year like Call of Duty, Gears of War, Apex, and Metro, I was curious as I had never played a DMC game. I got it on sale and endeavored to give it a try.
From the moment the opening sequence began, I was hooked. Even with only the basic knowledge of game lore provided, the story drew me in with its rapid-fire pacing and high-speed action, starting from the end of the very first cutscene. I quickly grew invested in characters with and of whom I had no previous experience or knowledge, though at times dialogue felt forced for the sake of unnecessary exposition, which was often provided redundantly through flashbacks.
The game's greatest strength, its combat, also serves to hinder it at times. In comparison to the purity and fluidity with which the most combat-intensive portions play, many of the other simpler sections of platforming or exploration can feel dull by comparison.
That's not to say that the combat holds the game back, on the contrary. The developers were definitely aware that the combat was the true keystone feature of the game, and they make excellent use of it. The combat never once feels stale or repetitive, and every character plays in a totally different manner. Unlike many other games, the combat can allow even the clumsiest, most button-mashing noobs such as myself to pull off awesome combo chains through the use of the auto-chain feature, something which I have not seen in other games. The combat itself is incredibly responsive and has better feedback than any game in recent memory for me. This is underscored by the game's sound design, providing real meaty THWACKS alongside the games excellent soundtrack. At the normal difficulties, the game is perhaps slightly too easy, to the point that an uninitiated such as myself can make it more than 3/4 of the way through the game without dying. Perhaps this is not the case on higher difficulties, but as this review was written during my first playthrough, I am not yet certain.
At no point during this game have I felt that it was at all undeserving of the hype which it has received. Perhaps someone with more investment into the series may feel otherwise, but as my first DMC game this has served both as an excellent introduction and to ignite my interest in the other games in the series. A firm recommendation to all who will listen, and an easy choice for one of my favorite games of 2019.

XFlame{IN}
32 products in account
3
19 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 6

Recommended
91.1 hrs on record
Posted: August 2, 2019
Product received for free

The Story:

-This game continues where the 4th game left off. Yes, you heard that right, it changes the timeline so that the 2nd game is not the last. The story ties up almost all of the loose ends made by the other games in a nice fashion and the ending is ♥♥♥♥♥♥ beautiful too. To me this is how story making in games should be done.
-This journey, like in the 4th game is mostly about Nero and kind of putting the focus on his arc, but what sets it apart is that it actually does it well this time and also does a great job finishing the sibling rivalry of Dante and Vergil.

The World/Level Design:
-I'm quite disappointed at what was in here. I feel like they had much more freedom with what they could do in the missions that it's just a lost opportunity. I loved the design of Mission 2 but that design fades away after like 3 missions and then from there it's just Casual bloody corridor number 21234.
-There are aspects of job well done in these levels but it's the overuse of them that kind of tires me out.

The Character Design (and use of Trish and Lady in the story):
-The character designs are truly phenomenal,very distinct and memorable. All the way from Nero & Dante to even the enemies.
-Not only is this a huge plus for newcomers to the franchise as they will remmember these legendary protagonists, but is also a huge help with the combat (which I will talk about further down).
-Now I didn't know where to put this so I guess I'll cram it in here. I'm truly disappointed at how they handled Trish and Lady. They both have like 5 lines in the whole game, one fight scene, and literally have no point in the story. If you ask me, I would be fine with them saying: oh they got captured and then you save them at the end, so they wouldn't even need to focus on them.
The Voices:
-From Johnny Yong Bosch, Daniel Southworth and all the way to the phenomenal japanese voice actor Toshiyuki Morikawa (who also does Kira Yoshikage in Jojo's Bizzare Adventure).
-All of the voice actors do a great job at making the characters feel fleshed out and alive. You can feel the love and passion they put in every scene and that just deserves respect. (Not to mention that Daniel is actually quite a decent guy outside of his job, the man is just amazing.)

The Soundtrack:
-Dmc has always had a killer soundtrack. (well, I guess it mostly depends on your taste)
-From the new soundtrack Devil Trigger, to the old Public Enemy and Out of my Way, they do an amazing job at the execution.
-Not only do they make new killer tracks, but they pay respects to all of the old ones which is a huge plus in my book.
-Each soundtrack is made to ramp up as you ramp up the combat, to make your adrenaline pump even harder and elevates the gameplay to even greater proportions.

The Gameplay:
-I would like to stress this out as much as I can, altough I probably can't stress it out enough. This franchise has the best combat system that has ever been made. From the many variations you can do,t o how the combos flow seamlessly one into another while the music is kicking in the background and you finish it off with that taunt at the perfect moment when the song stops. There is no better feeling then that.
-The Upgrade System is not anything new, as returning players are familiar with it from Dmc 4 most likely. The upgrades themselves aren't all on the new side, there are plenty of upgrades that are the same as in Dmc 4 and then added on top of them are the new ones.
Nero's Gameplay:
-Nero has gotten much more complex due to introduction of the Devil Arms. Powerful arms, which can change how you play and interact with enemies on multiple levels.
-From the Exceed mechanic that powers all of your attacks if timed correctly, to the devil arm combos and on top of all of that add the Devil Trigger mechanic and the use of just normal combos, and players can find themselves quite overwhelmed as to what move to choose for that Smoking Sick Style.
-Nero is my favorite out of the 3 currently playable characters. I simply love how he interacts with the environment and the enemies in many fun ways, from the Devil Trigger to even using your Taunt to kick enemies.
-I also want to touch on his character development throughout the game. They did an outstanding job with Nero in my opinion. He went from being this boy who gets mad and wants more POWER! to a man that just wants to protect and unite his family.
Dante's Gameplay:
-Now, if someone had the time to sit here all day reading my reviews, I would go into detail why Dante is the most complex video game character ever made, but I'm going to try and make it short and sweet.
-Dante is the hardest to play out of the 3, due to him having so many options in combat and being able to change your weapons and playstyle on the fly, changing how Dante works with the press of a single button is something else, but to be able to master this man is quite insane.
-In my opinion Dmc 5 Dante is much easier to play than his Dmc 4 counterpart, and thats a good thing for the casual players. (I will touch on this topic more below)
-Storywise, Dante is still the lovable, charming and silly guy that he is. Honestly, all the character development has been done and you would think they wouldn't put that much time into him, but you would be wrong, as they elevated his arc into something beautiful too. His arc is put to an "end" here in a satisfying way that I am content with, this being the final game in the franchise.

The new guy V:
-Plenty of people seem to love V for his, on the outside, edgy anime protagonist personality, but the soft and nerdy one on the inside look, and I must say they are all wrong.
-The reason V is a good character is how he contrasts the gameplay of Nero & Dante in a fun way, how he handles himself in situations unknown to him and how his new combat system works.
-All in all V was, and is a good addition to the roster and I will miss him if another game comes out.
Combat system in general:
-As I have mentioned above, when talking about Dante, the game been made "easier" so that the more casual players can get into it and not feel as overwhelmed. I, for one, am aboard. If you want a challange, just go to a higher difficulty and there, problem solved.
-What I am not a fan of, is that they removed the "Inertia" mechanic. I won't go into detail on this mechanic, as it alone makes the game 10x more complex. This mechanic alone is why I think that Dmc 4 has the better combat system for the super invested and advanced players such as Donguri99, Blue Devil, Milz and others. With "Inertia", so many things are made possible and I am truly sorry that I can't go further into detail, but take my word for it.

Conclusion:
-Devil May Cry 5 is an outstanding game. It might not live up to the combat complexity of Dmc 4, for the invested players but for the casual players and long running fans of the series, this is without a doubt, a very polished masterpiece that no one would mind playing over it's counterpart.
-From the story, to the music, the character and enemy design, and the amazing combat system, Hideaki Itsuno has made his very own gem in the gaming industry that will be remembered as one of gaming's best, and fans will remember him as the man who did the impossible.

The Saltiest Wizard
356 products in account
0
19 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 0

Recommended
57.1 hrs on record
Posted: December 9, 2019
More than 10 years of waiting since the release of DMC4... You could say that this game was my "Half Life 3," so to speak. And while I preordered it and played it on day 1, I've been hesitant to write my review for quite a while. The reason is simple - I've been giving Capcom a chance to unveil this game's full potential through some DLC that the community has been asking for, but sadly, our pleas were left ignored. So we're most likely stuck waiting for Special Edition's release, that'll most likely happen along with the release of new consoles.
With that said, I do still hope that Capcom won't force this SE ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ on us for the fourth time in franchise history, and I will be happy to update my review should they release new content, but for now let's have a look at what DMC5 shaped up to be, and whether it managed to live up to it's hype.
Overview
True to its name, DMC5 delivers exactly what you expect from it - amazing, fast-paced, engaging and challenging gameplay, accompanied by fantastic soundtrack and some really good graphics. The characters are as badass as ever (don't mention DmC, we don't talk about it here), and the overall story is... well, okayish. The story never was a particularly strong point of this franchise, save for, perhaps, DMC3; and the fifth entry, sadly, doesn't blow your mind in any way, either.
Story
Diving a bit deeper into the story, I have to say that this is arguably the weakest aspect of the game. The story's pace, the way it starts, the way it just constantly jumps back and forth the different characters and moments of time, and the fact that this time around, we have three playable characters... It just feels rushed, both in terms of pace and production. The standard 20 missions just don't cut it anymore; they just can't give enough screen (and play) time for all characters. And I haven't even mentioned the ending. I do not wish to spoil anything, but let me just put it like this: the ending felt as if the devs were forced to wrap things up ASAP and just let the potential for much more character development and drama go to waste. It can even be felt in the last two missions design, since they are... Well, 
Gameplay
Luckily, gameplay in the fifth game is arguably the best it ever was. That's right, my friends, even in its current state I'm ready to say that DMC5 surpasses both DMC3 - the most beloved game in the series - and DMC4SE, with it's biggest roster of playable characters yet. DMC5 takes the best elements of DMC4 and even some of the reboot's good practices, presenting us with a really great and diverse experience. The three playable characters each feel significantly different and unique. Nero feels like a solid upgrade over his version in DMC4 (both in terms of gameplay and character, actually), now relying on his new prosthetic arms, which essentially serve as powerful consumables. Dante feels like the most badass devil hunter there is, with four battle styles to master, 4 melee and 4 ranged weapons to choose from, as well as some powerful new abilities that almost make him feel like Sparda's equal. He feels the most challenging to play as, motivating you to start learning all his mechanics and not just stick to one preferred playstyle. And finally, V, the newcomer. Surprisingly enough, I liked this character far more than I originally thought I will. Again, this goes for both him as the playable character and the character in the story. His playstyle feels, by far, the most unique. It still feels close to standard DMC gameplay, but the whole idea of him using his familiars, rather than fighting himself, adds a whole new layer. And don't let yourself get fooled by the power of his familiars - on lower difficulties, his gameplay does feel a bit like button mashing and keeping a safe distance, but if you wish to give yourself some challenge, I highly recommend you to try playing as him on higher difficulties; you'll learn that this character is by no means invincible. The only real disappointment is that he feels the most rushed, with the least amount of missions to try him out in action and most limited moveset.
Another aspect of gameplay worth mentioning is "coop," of course. For some reason, instead of giving us option of legit coop experience, Capcom gave us a stupid cameo system straight from Resident Evil. Translation - you may encounter other players, but in most cases you won't even be able to interact with them. And the only TWO(!) moments when you can actually play along with them last for about 5 minutes or so.
Graphics
Not much to say here - the graphics are fantastic. The new, more photorealistic style served this game surprisingly well, even though the previous chapters looked more like your standard, final fantasy-like, anime style games. The characters were redesigned a bit to fit this new style better and again, they actually ended up quite likeable. Weapon and enemies design is great, visual effects are amazing, and the only thing that is a bit disappointing is level design. The levels feel way too similar visually, with half of them taking place in a wrecked city, covered in demonic tree's roots, while the other half takes place in... well, the demonic tree mentioned above. Not much to look at, sadly.
Sound
Again, true to it's name, DMC5 delivers solid voice acting, solid sound design and phenomenal soundtrack. The only thing that I can highlight about sound is the new feature that changes the pace of track based on your current style level. It is both a great innovation and a bit of a letdown: while you actually enjoy the game reacting to you playing well, and you get motivated to keep your style level at max, the length of the song gets quite reduced, because you only get to hear a fraction of it that is designated to your particular style level. Another drawback of this system is that it only works for the new tracks, so if you bought the deluxe edition, don't expect the tracks from old games to behave the same way. And another personal complaint of mine - even with a bunch of tracks now available, there's no way to making your own tracklist for each character. You can only choose one battle theme for each.

Conclusion
DMC5 may yet become the best game in the series. It is a really great game in it's current state, but it's just a bit rushed. It feels that the team was eager to deliver more, but the deadlines limited their creativity. If I were given a choice of either getting this game the time it actually came out, or to wait another year for it, I would undoubtedly choose to wait. This game needs more missions, it needs proper coop, and it could definitely use more playable characters (or a certain playable character, at the very least). I genuinely hope that this game's full potential will be fully realised, one way or another. And once this time comes, I will be glad to edit this review accordingly. =)
Until then, 8/10, even though it should've been a 9. Why not 10, though, you ask? Because a 10/10 game in my opinion is something worth recommending to literally everyone, regardless of their preferences. And DMC has always been a bit of a niche franchise. This is the same reason why I can't call it a GOTY material (tbh, I don't think there was any game that truly deserved the GOTY 2019 title, and it is most certainly not Sekiro). But if you're looking for a great slasher game, or just want to give DMC franchise a try - you have my total approval, although if you care about the story, I would suggest you start with DMC3.

P.S. A well-deserved "Best action game of 2019" title. Let us keep our fingers on our Devil Triggers crossed and hope that Capcom will give this game some much needed content updates as soon as possible.

Recommended
29.9 hrs on record
Posted: November 9, 2019
Rating: 8.5/10
Genre: Action Adventure

The Good:
+ Levels are well designed with great aesthetics. The levels are linear in nature, however there are a few times when you can go off the path and explore and discover a hidden secret. Although the levels are linear the developers did a good job of constantly changing the environments or throwing a new enemy at you to keep you on your toes.

+ 3 separate characters each with their own combat systems, weapons and style. In some levels you can choose who you want to play as but most of the time, each level is constructed around a particular character in mind.

+ The combat system is where this game really seems to shine. The system is designed with both newcomers and experts alike. For those like myself that just want to play casually to a degree will find enough here to enjoy and those looking for something more can master more complex systems and become amazing. The game includes an ‘auto assist’ mode for those who really want a casual experience where the game will automatically string together some very impressive looking combos. Although personally I found that mode takes away a lot of the fun.

+ Almost every level features a unique boss that looks great and fun to play against. Bosses make sure you use of the combat system more effectively and forces you to play a bit more defensively than you normally would.

+Bloody palace is an option that becomes unlocked after you beat the game where you have to battle 100 floors of enemies. Good for those looking for more of a hardcore challenge.

+ 6 difficulty modes and some of the higher modes completely change the enemy placement.

+ Good soundtrack

The Average:
+/- The game has lots of loading, go to menu screen…loading…watch cutscene…loading…begin level…loading. The good news is, the loading is fast so its not really too much of a problem.

+/- Story is decent and requires little knowledge of previous events although it certainly helps as things can get convoluted. DMC5 features a helpful video explaining the past events of the previous games.

Conclusion:
A very accessible game that’s fun to play and soak in all the over the top action drama while you hack and slash grotesque enemies to a rock soundtrack.

93.4 hrs on record
Posted: June 15, 2020
DMC 5 is the action game that all action games want to be.

It provides a deep and endless combat system without compromising in graphics and the presentation of its story. The gameplay is boundless and there is always something new to experiment with, master, and learn. There is so much to mess around with, and the game is happy for you to break it in ways that are only limited by your own creativity. No matter what level of player you are, the game makes you feel both powerful and stylish.

For DMC fans this is the conclusion to the stories and threads left unfinished by Capcom for the last 10 years between DMC 4 and DMC 5, and it is a satisfying one. Unfortunately, my main gripe with it is that the story is NOT newcomer-friendly story wise. DMC 5 is very self-indulgent with callbacks and references to DMC games, manga, anime and spinoffs. The impact of the story and many elements within it WILL be lost on a newcomer to a series. I recommend playing or watching the stories of all the games (except DMC2) before playing DMC5.

Oh yeah, Capcom also has some deceptive microtransactions that serve as early unlocks or additional ingame currency that DON'T add to the gameplay at all and aren't necessary, a bit of a rubbish move there.

All in all, DMC 5 is a ridiculously good game. After all this time, Capcom finally gives DMC the budget it deserves and we have this game that ticks every box for long time fans and new players interested in action games. I keep coming back to this game again and again and I just can't stop.It is THAT good.

Recommended
129.5 hrs on record
Posted: August 1, 2020
This review comes from someone who grew up with the series and played 3,4 and DmC 2013 so many times I can barely count.

I have invested 2 months of almost daily playing into the game on my PS4 before I got into pc gaming, so sadly I don't have the hours I actually played this game.

Basically, for 5 Capcom took everything we liked from previous titles gameplay wise and put it into one game. There is nothing more satisfying when you're finally done getting every skill for the 3 playable characters or the one you enjoy the most and you start seeing your improvment with the combos and the whole playing system - especially for new fans. 5 feels like one of the most friendliest for newcommers the series has ever had.

The effects are so so stunning. The RE engine is literally reason I'm saving up for a better graphic card. The cutscenes are a LOT which I personally enjoyed. It feels like a small movie, while older DMC games where a lot of playing and less cutscenes. This is something that depens on preference! It is not overwhelming, yet a good amount.
Another factor I really appreciate is that for the returning main characters, Dante, Vergil and Nero, the voice actors stayed the same. If you're a fan, this particular aspect feels different. I had a lot of flashbacks from 10 year old me smashing buttons in DMC4.

The only negative thing 5 has to me is how it handles 3 playable characters. It bugs me a little that you cannot decide for every mission who you want to play. Don't get me wrong, I enjoyed both Dante and Nero's gameplay - V not so much, but that is a preference thing once again - but whenever you get good at one style or a certain move (Dante: Aggressive and offensive, Nero: A lot of timing and basically air fighting, V: defensive), you get pulled out of it, since you now have to play a different character. The only moments you can choose are Mission 7 between Nero and V and Mission 13 between all 3, to adjust to your personal fighting style. It really bugs me, but it is something you can avoid once you've played through the game or one difficulty. I don't complain much about it since I cannot change it, but it is worth noting. What I do is just play the levels of one characters so that I keep the same fighting style for longer than 1-2 hours.

Another noteworthy thing is that 5 brings a lot of the story from 1 to 4 together. Basically this means: A lot of people who aren't fan of the series won't understand a lot of hidden things and both obvious things happening. 5's plot feels like after the 11 year pause the creators wanted to put a point to a lot of things that have happened in the past or are left unanswered and finally fill them with answers. This leads to the fact that, of course, if you're new and haven't had all these questions since you haven't seen the things to raise questions, you might feel like the story is underwhelming.
Even as a big fan I think it is. The plot is easily summed up in a few words and not a lot happens if you look at it in a neutral way, but if you watch it as someone who knows about the story, it feels satisfying to get answers to so many things.

TLDR: I love, love the game so much that I've just written my first review ever for a game so more people can see it. I'm a fan of two of capcom's most wellknown franchises, but I'm sad how much less known DMC is.

Recommended
4.4 hrs on record
Posted: October 29, 2021
This game saved my life, I'm playing this for the second time..

I am 28.

My ex-wife and I have a daughter together, and adopted our son together. They are now both 4 years old.

When we were going through our separation, I found myself lost and miserable. I was self destructive. I got so mad one day from everything spiraling out of my control that I punched some concrete in a moment of overwhelming emotion. That caused me to break my 5th metacarpal in my right hand... my working hand... my games hand.. the hand that I held and carried my children to bed with.. The hand I desperately needed to make sure I could continue to provide.

After learning of the severity of my self-inflicted damage, I was borderline suicidal. Keep in mind that just a few months before this, I was the happiest man with no history of depression or anxiety. I have never had fits of rage, or been one to break down and cry, but I was in a low spot that just really buried me from being able to see the light on the other side.

Having nothing better to do, I searched for a game I could play, ONE HANDED while I recovered. I somehow stumbled upon this game and read some of the reviews. I decided that it had to be worth a shot... I must admit, I didn't beat the game, or play nearly as long as some of you. In fact, I may have only played this game a day or two.. With that being said, after doing so, I had a new found joy and hope for life. I was able to put behind me the pain and suffering that had been cast over me. I was able to experience other peoples joy and happiness. I was able to see the fruits of my "labor". I relaxed for 5 ♥♥♥♥♥♥♥ minutes to this music long enough to realize that I was going to be okay.

After coming to that realization, I turned the game off, and I went back to work. It hurt my hand like hell but I was motivated. I stopped feeling so damn sorry for myself, and I became the father I needed to be in that moment, not the weak boy I was behaving as.

Today, I am close friend with my kids mother. We don't fight, or argue, or say hurtful things to each other. We are parents, and friends.

I now have 3 kids. My third child is, wait for it, ALSO 4 YEARS OLD. The woman I am with was going through a very similar situation at the time of my own separation, and we just stumbled in to each others life unexpectedly. We have been in a relationship for a year now, and are very happy together.

Moral of the story, you never know what life holds in store for you, and if I would have given up when all the odds were stacked against me, I wouldn't be where I am today. This amazing game helped me realize that.

That's all, thank you for reading it,

Recommended
51.7 hrs on record
Posted: May 10, 2021
DMC5 is just a blast.
The combat is the main selling point of this game. There is just no other game with combat like this. It is just so satisfying and fun to defeat the enemies with style.
For me, there is one aspect of the game that is even better than the combat. This is the music. Songs like "Devil Trigger" and "Bury The Light" are the reason I learned about this game in the first place. Bury The Light is one of my favorite songs of all time now. It really deserves the title of "The New Rules of Nature."
The story of DMC5 is actually better than I expected after talking to some friends about it. Sure it's not super profound or filled with a lot of things that make you reflect on it, but it is still a well written story. It's like a page turner book where you keep wanting to learn more and more and as more and more things are revealed you go, "Oooh so it was that all along!"
Overall, DMC5 is a fantastic game with stellar game play, a story that is gripping but not too deep, and music that is so good its worth buying the game just to hear it. Give DMC5 a try - it's a Smokin' Sexy great game!

16.2 hrs on record
Posted: March 1, 2021
A refreshing jaunt into the land of hack-n-slash, DMCV brings the once-thought-dead series and genre back from the grave and in top form, with flowing combat and stunning visuals for a modern age.

However apparently as a punishment for piracy, Capcom has denied PC players the ability to purchase the Special Edition upgrade of the game, which is currently locked as a next-gen console exclusive only, which brought about two new gamemodes; Turbo Mode and Last Dark Knight Mode, as well as Ray Tracing and other graphical upgrades, on top of Vergil as a new playable character. You can purchase Vergil as a standalone DLC for the PC/Last Gen Console, but that's it.

The only way Turbo/LDK mode can be played on PC is via community made mods that are faithful recreations of these modes. Which also usually break every time Capcom pushes out a patch for the PC version. If you wanna deal with setting up third party modding tools, dealing with installation and management of them, more power to you. And for the Ray tracing/graphical upgrade mods for PC... there are no mods. Yet.

If you own a next-gen console, just go buy the game there, I guess. Otherwise it's up to you. The game is pretty cheap now at only $25, compared to the $60 it was at launch.

Also worth noting, the game is notoriously short. I understand Hack N' Slashes get their value through constant replayability, honing your skills and turning combat into a flowing spectacle of death, but this game made me feel like I was left high and dry after beating it the first time. My exact words on getting to the ending was "Hold on, is that really it? It's done already?" The entire game comes off as one massive bait for the inevitably way cooler sequel Capcom is gonna squeeze out some point in the future, and that DMCV was just testing the consumer waters a bit.

DedVice
56 products in account
0
23 people found this review helpful
3 people found this review funny 0

Recommended
11.0 hrs on record
Posted: February 20, 2020
Like my reviews? Go follow my Curator page.

While I've been familiar with this series for ages, Devil May Cry V was the first game in the series I've played. While I like hack-n-slash games, I don't have much experience with them outside of loving Metal Gear Rising: Revengeance and playing a bit of Bayonetta, so I didn't really know what to expect. What I initially started playing as a "side game" to lift my spirits whenever A Plague Tale: Innocence got too emotionally overwhelming, ended up taking over the majority of my gaming free time, and caused me to put Plague Tale on the backburner. It really leans into the "game" part of video games, feeling very reminiscent of DOOM 2016's mentality of "gameplay first, story later", and it ended up being an incredibly fun experience once things started to click.

Graphics

The visuals are not the highlight by any stretch, but they're pretty solid for the most part. The characters look amazing obviously, with an incredible level of detail put into them. The same can be said about the environments, however I will say that I wish the game had more variety in the levels themselves. They all feel very similar, either going the route of being city ruins or the inside of the demons' domain. While it makes sense from a story perspective, as well as it being somewhat alleviated towards the end, I still wish they did more with the environments in this game considering how high quality the visuals themselves are. Surprisingly, I thought the game did a surprisingly good job of not overwhelming the player with visual effects, which I thought would get overbearing due to the emphasis on style and the general absurdity of these games. Overall, the visuals were good, although I wish they had some more variety.

Gameplay

Of course, if you're looking into buying this kind of game, the gameplay is the most crucial aspect to that. And thankfully, Devil May Cry V delivers in spades. There is an insane amount of depth and fluidity to the combat, which gets multiplied when considering that you're playing three different characters throughout the campaign. The quality of the combat alone makes the price of admission worthwhile, and the game knows this. Like DOOM, it focuses almost solely on combat, almost to a fault depending on who you ask. However, this didn't really bother me, because the game's focus on customization means that you can easily change your playstyle on the fly and still get rewarded for it, so while you're restricted to basically nothing but combat, the combat doesn't restrict you. The bosses were also quite enjoyable, and considering some of the horror stories I've heard about some of the bosses in this series, I felt they were almost all consistently good, and were simply mediocre at worst. As far as criticisms go, I will reiterate my wish that the levels had some more variety in them in terms of design (maybe different gimmicks in combat like hazards). I also felt like the parts of the game where you had to play as V weren't as interesting and also exponentially more painful due to the nature of his playstyle, but this is mostly alleviated considering that you're only required to play him for a few chapters. Overall, while I have my criticisms of the gameplay, I can set them aside considering just how incredibly smooth, deep, and plain entertaining the combat is.

Story

The story isn't particularly good, but it didn't really take itself seriously so I had some fun with it at least. There were a few times where I felt like things just happened so the plot can move forward, and there were quite a few characters thrown to the wayside that I thought were pretty major figures in the series, namely Lady and Trish. I also wish some things were more coherently explained (like a certain turning point and major reveal towards the end of the game), but again, I didn't really have any level of expectation for the story. Could it have been a little more thorough in its story while still not taking itself seriously? I think so. And while I can forgive the story for being sort of weak considering how absurd it is, it still feels just a tad bit underdeveloped and could've benefited from an extra scene or two. However, this is not a dealbreaker by any stretch, and is more of a mild gripe than anything.

Audio

The music is fine. Some of it feels like a mess of aggressive noises to "pump you up" or whatever, but certain tunes were quite enjoyable. "Devil Trigger" alone brings this game's audio score up quite a bit, though. The voice acting's pretty good, with everyone doing a pretty good job of leaning into their stereotypical aspects of their character to add to the silliness of the story. There isn't much else to say. Everything that isn't "Devil Trigger" is just fine, I guess.

Content Value

While the game is quite short and there isn't much you can do to make playthroughs different on a basic level, the addition of harder difficulties paired with the aforementioned incredible combat means that you can absolutely get some more out of this game than just a single playthrough. While I have not tested this myself, I believe that harder difficulties give enemies new attacks and do more than just bloat their health and damage, which could further incentivize you to play through the game multiple times. There's absolutely some replay value here that is more than just player-motivated if you enjoy the combat system enough.

Verdict

In conclusion, there isn't a lot to say about Devil May Cry 5 outside of its gameplay. It's an extremely well-made hack-n-slash game that loves leaning in to its sillier side. It's absolutely worth it just for the combat alone, but it's a game that can be simply described as fun. And for a critic like me that often finds meaning in games deeper than just what level of entertainment do they provide, it's nice to have a game like this every so often. Definitely worth a try.

Graphics - 9.0/10
Gameplay - 10/10
Story - 6.5/10
Audio - 8.0/10
Content Value - 8.0/10

.:8.6/10:.
"Great"

+ Incredible combat system
+ Stunning graphics
+ Devil Trigger
+ Surprisingly high replay value
+ Lots of creativity and depth

- Lack of variety in level design
- Some underdeveloped story aspects

Recommended
12.7 hrs on record
Posted: December 21, 2021
While I did enjoy the game, I felt like it was lacking something, though it's hard to describe what. The presentation is insanely good and the gameplay is fun, but the story is meh and ends on a rather sudden note. The levels are almost all very dark and broody, which I suppose fits the mood, but they lack variety. More levels like the first two or three would have been nice, but they quickly devolve into "dark hallways" or "dark demon places" for the rest of the game.

In the end, a bit more variety in level design would be nice, especially since there is not much exploration either. I also felt like there was some lack of variety in combat, both in terms of enemy types and moves, though I am probably not good enough at the game to really rate that well. The game felt repetitive somewhat quickly, but also isn't really long enough for that to be a huge problem.

For a fun, short, action-filled romp in DMC fashion, you can't go wrong, but I personally enjoyed both DMC games I played before this - DMC 4 and even the previous DMC re-imagining - quite a bit more, though it is hard to put my finger on exactly why. Still quite fun though and the soundtrack is great, so I don't regret my playthrough.

Dante
188 products in account
3
6 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 0

Recommended
23.8 hrs on record
Posted: September 6, 2021
A largely triumphant return to form for the first and foremost character action series. While I didn't outright hate what some consider to be the completely disastrous reboot from Ninja Theory, the issues with its characterization and writing were insurmountable. That is far less of a problem in DMC 5, a fine example to other large gaming companies of what happens when you just cut the malarkey and give fans what they want.

For those unfamiliar, DMC is the sometimes edgy, sometimes cheesy, and always entertaining story of twin brothers, Dante and Vergil, the sons of legendary demon swordsman Sparda and his human wife Eva. The first game saw you control only Dante, but each iteration since has added additional playable characters with increasingly divergent gameplay from our white-haired, red-coated, wisecracking leading man. In each iteration, you battle demon hordes and bosses using a mixture of firearms and demonic melee weaponry, obtain red orbs to purchase new moves and attacks, and progress through gothic and hellish environments in various states of disrepair. Many characters can activate a signature super mode called "Devil Trigger", enhancing their attacks and often making new ones temporarily available. The series as a rule is difficult to play and even more so to play well, relying on a combo system where varying your moves and avoiding taking damage increases your ranking. As a kid playing the first game, I barely scraped through Easy Auto my first time playing and with practice and repeated playthroughs, I was eventually able to beat the game on Hard.

This fifth numbered entry sees the return of Dante and Nero, a young gun, with a demonic right arm, a very large revolver, a sword with a motorcycle engine built into it and a chip on his shoulder, first introduced in DMC 4. Joining them is newcomer V, a sickly goth with a penchant for poetry and controlling demons to do the fighting for him. Together, they must stop the growth of the Qliphoth- an enormous, destructive demonic tree that has taken root in Red Grave city, a blighted burg with a connection to the heroes' past. The story features at least token appearances by characters, enemies and references events throughout the series, including the anime and even the light novels, and even deigns to mention DMC 2 in its "Previously on DMC" cutscene, a game almost totally ignored otherwise by both Capcom and series fans.

DMC 5 is probably the biggest and most diverse offering in the series to date, with a total of four different playable characters if you include the Vergil DLC, a 20 mission campaign, a bunch of secret missions, a full wave survival mode the series calls "Bloody Palace", and even a training area where you can try out new moves before purchase and adjust enemy types and behaviors to see the resulting effects. It also includes a sort of half-assed coop mode where any time the characters would cross paths in the campaign missions, the role of whichever characters you're not playing can be taken by random other players, with the option to have the game prioritize people from your friends list.

DMC 5 is at once more accessible then earlier titles, especially the first and second games, and also harder. Gold Orbs, used to revive your player to full health are much more plentiful then before, and you can even receive extra ones if other players rate you as "stylish" after playing with them, so you are far less likely to get an actual game over and have to restart a mission- which is good, because DMC 5 stops playing around at about mission 14, and I was unable to finish most missions after that, even with the intentionally overpowered Vergil, without using at least one Gold Orb, usually during boss fights. The last few bosses are similar to those of Monster Hunter World, with heavy attacks that knock you around with few openings for you to attack between them. In addition, there are fewer ways to safely cheese most fights that you could do in earlier entries, such as when I used Ebony & Ivory, Dante's twin pistols, exclusively to chip down the health of the Cerberus boss in DMC 3.

While many enemies can be safely pummeled into oblivion without fear of reprisal, especially when using Vergil's Yamato sword, A few enemies are much harder to stagger and will force you to start paying attention to what you're doing, and if you can't parry them with timed attacks of your own, block using Dante's Royalguard style, grab them out of their animation with Nero's Devil Breaker arm, etc, or just keep your distance, you're going to have to get good at dodging, and dodging in DMC is honestly rather awkward in comparison to some games due to its revolving around the game's lock on system. There is seemingly no simple backdodge move, though some characters can do so as part of a "step back and then dash in as a counter" move. More likely you'll have to side dodge or jump over an attack, and some attacks cannot be evaded by one or the other, or can even be evaded at all if you're too close. Reading enemy movements and tells becomes paramount as you progress.

Finishing DMC 5 on the default "Devil Hunter" difficulty was ultimately not too stressful except maybe for my thumbs, though having used 6ish Gold Orbs in both vanilla and Vergil mode I have to wonder how good I actually was at the game. Good enough to not run out of Gold Orbs, I suppose. DMC 5 wants you to finish its story, but if you want to get good and say, S rank every mission or play on harder difficulties, thats on you.

I didn't buy DMC 5 when it first released. In fact I waited on it for quite a while, not only because of the typical price of a new AAA release but because of the presence of Denuvo DRM, later patched out, the presence of which is infamous for causing system issues on many people's computers. As a friend of mine often points out, Capcom occasionally does the right thing for their games- they just seldom learn from the experience.

DMC 5 is a good time over all and I recommend it to both series veterans and those looking to get into the character/stylish action genre for the first time, as it has something to offer both and probably most folks in between, if you can handle a game that's a bit harder then some. I can assure you that you'll fare better then the typical paid reviewer, at least, if you are capable of paying even a modicum of attention. You'll also get to hear a certain oft-memed and very catchy fight theme.

The Vergil DLC is also worth a purchase, playing him lets you effortlessly breeze through most encounters and even some bosses that gave me pause as the other characters, though last two missions are just as challenging, if not more so, then playing them in the base game. He has access to the same set of weapons used in the Special Edition release of DMC 3, but with a host of new moves for each, a doppleganger summon, a "concentration" bar that allows him to build attack damage through landing successful attacks and avoiding damage, and hilariously powerful, screen-clearing finishers. However, Vergil's missions do not use the coop "link" function.

Jiyo
109 products in account
0
7 people found this review helpful
1 person found this review funny 0

Recommended
136.9 hrs on record
Posted: December 25, 2020
If you want to play an action game that feels rewarding from when you first start out 'til you become a complete master, this is it right here.

Story
If you know nothing about the Devil May Cry series, you don't need to play the previous ones for story, as story isn't the main point of the Devil May Cry series and neither are you missing out on any important narrative exposition. The story is purposefully written to be campy, but also fun at the same time, so don't expect a nobel prize for literature, just sit back and have fun with it.

Audio
There isn't much to say about the audio other than praise. None of the sound effects are annoying, there are even audio cues to help with hearing enemies being summoned, dodging enemies and even timing your combos. The music is 10/10. I enjoy listening to all the characters themes (yes even Dante's) Most of the community / fan base from what I see also highly praise the OST.

Game Play
For some, the because you can complete the main campaign in about 6 hours on average for new players (maybe less) they don't see the game as having much replay value. The replay value isn't about playing the campaign, it's about challenging yourself to higher difficulties and trials. As you play the game and play the different characters, you'll start to get better at their toolkit, you'll see and understand enemy attack patters and you'll devise stylish / efficient ways to beat them. The game play is fun enough that you'll want to see how far you can go with your skills in the game even past playing the campaign once. You'll want to play it the second time on the higher difficulty. Heck you may even try bloody palace, which is a 100 floors of increasing difficult challenges. Once you become very familiar with your character and fighting mobs / bosses, you'll start to not only survive, but style on them, and let me tell you, there is a huge rush of dopamine killing a boss without getting hit and achieving the highest rank on something you once struggled with.

tldr
If you're the type of person that doesn't want a challenge, there isn't much replay value in this game for you, especially if you aren't a fan of the DMC series.

Not Recommended
10.6 hrs on record
Posted: July 10, 2019
I'm at mission 18 and I'm a little surprised this game gets such high praises. So far, I am really disappointed by this game and can't recommend it. I mean yea it has nice graphics and the combat is good, but... ohh well

Cons
-For me DMC is much more than just combat. I loved gothic style of DMC1/3 with light metroidvania level design. Sadly, DMC5 doesn't have anything of that. It's almost exclusively narrow corridors between combat arenas where you simply has to get from point A to B, and sadly, it gets boring and repetitive at mission 3 already. Not to mention, that there are only two settings: City (first part of the game) and Demon-Construction-ish (second part), which makes every level feel the same. The Demon-Construction is the worst offender, because the whole environment is using the same texture. Overall, it's the worst level design in the series so far.
-Combat, while good, didn't change in almost any way compared to DMC4. Dante is basically the same as in 4, the same moveset with just some very minor changes and new weapons. Nero will probably get one additional ability later in the game, but so far, he is basically the same as in previous game. V is really cool and different form other characters, but his moveset is clearly underdeveloped.
-Only one memorable boss fight so far

Pros
+many enemies return from previous entries, which makes this game bestiary a collection of "the best of DMC" with some nice additions and modifications, and I'm perfectly fine with that.
+cutscenes are really well done

Split
+/- many bosses and sub bosses, but they fail to be memorable
+/- V playstyle
+/- online component - it's cool to see other characters do their story thing in the background of your level (controlled by other players), but this is hugely underdeveloped feature. You will hardly ever actually see them (but you know they are there, because of message in the corner), and their action have no consequences in your level (you don't actually help each other in any way) - unless there is actually a way to play levels together - but I didn't discover it yet

Recommended
115.9 hrs on record
Posted: March 24, 2019
DMC 5 is the best DMC in almost every way.
+Slightly easier to pull off advanced moves/combos than in other DMCs
+Nero now has 12 devil breakers to choose from and each comes with different abilities such as electric blasts, anti-armor drill, and evasive propulsion.
+DMC 5 uses the RE engine, the same engine used in Resident Evil 2 remake.
+Easiest DMC in the series by far, good for those looking for less challenge
+There aren't many major story developments, but the developments that do occur are major. Many claim Nero is more like-able in DMC 5 than in 4.

-For DMC vets looking for a challenge, DMC 5 is way too easy and boring at times. On a no-item run, the difficulty picks up at the last boss on hard mode. DMD mode no item run is HARD and comparable to DMC 3's DMD mode.
-Uninspired enemy design
-Uninspired environments
-Most Bosses have no personality. They are mind-less demons out to destroy you.

This game is freaking awesome!

YouTube™ Video: Devil May Cry Story Summary - What You Need to Know to Play Devil May Cry 5! 
Views: 1,590,278
Support me on Patreon! https://www.patreon.com/suggestivegaming Follow me on Twitter! https://twitter.com/SuggestiveGames Dante and all his friends are back, baby!
I watched it a few times and was instantly involved in the lore and the characters. I promise you will love the game more if you know the lore.

About the game:
The game has 3 difficulties - Human, Devil hunter, and if you finish the game in DH mode, you unlock Son of Sparda mode, so there's tons of replayability and also tons of skills to be unlocked. Apart from that-

Recommended
100.5 hrs on record
Posted: March 9, 2019
What a game. Looks like CAPCOM have a good start in 2019.
RE 2 and now this?

DMC 5 not DmC . This is continuation that the fan deserved after DMC 4.
The storyline
The gameplay mechanic
The environment
The graphic
The soundtrack etc.

The introduction of V is quite refreshing where you fight with a summon beast/demon. I like it.
I enjoyed every piece of it from start to end. Really felt that my money worth.
No crash from start to end.

Although i do think that this game could be a bit overwhelming for new player who starts jumping into DMC series.
Especially playing Dante. Its a fast pace game where if you cant execute the right move quickly, you are wide open and enemy hit you. Even saw someone said this game is hard because there is no "evade button" .

If you are new to the series, take your time familiarizing the mechanic in training mode just to lock in the muscle memory.
Previous player from DMC4 knows well that the mechanic is still more or less the same from previous game.

Last but not least if you are DMC fans and cant buy it at full price, you damn sure need to buy it on sale.
